<Author>Renee001
<Content>Marriott ok, amenities misleading Overall the Marriott was a nice hotel, although it wasn't all it was cracked up to be. We traveled with 4 adults and one 15 month old and stayed in 2 rooms next to one another. The staff was very friendly and accomadating with switching rooms for a better view and trying to keep our rooms together. The concierge was our first disappointment..the first night they sent us to a restaurant that was closed, with no back up plan, it was a little annoying. Most irritating was that after asking them about the Caves(a 2 hour drive from the hotel). They told us that they were closed on Monday and Tuesday and gave us directions to go later in the week. When we drove out on Thursday we the gaurd at the gate informed us that the Caves have been closed for almost a year!!!! When we returned to the hotel the concierge told us that they had just found out it was closed that day....very irritating!As far as the amenities, the pool looked to be great for kids, only it is FREEZING! I think they must dump ice in it. You would very rarely see anyone in the pool(probably on their first day), and the hot tub was always full. Part of the problem is that the pool never gets full sun due to it's location, there is always a shadow over a majority of the pool. My poor son wanted so despirately to go in, but even he didn't last more that a few minutes before wanting out. The hotel does have a decent beach, but they don't mention that it's location is such that the water is extremely rough and swimming is not recommended. The waves are pretty big, and we witnessed people being bowled over by waves when they were just wading ankle deep.The location of the hotel was good, there are alot of restaurants nearby, and it is a very happening area. You really need a rental car, but be aware that parking is $16/day. If we were to do it over again, the best bet might to break your hotel stays up into 2 night stays around the island..that way you would get to see the whole island, and get the benefits of each area(like those with better beaches). Also, we went into La Concha Hotel and walked around...it seemed really nice and the pool felt a little warmer.

<Author>Travelover045
<Content>A Fun Vacation My husband, 6 year old daughter and I stayed here for 6 nights at the end of December 2008. After some initial annoyances, we could not get into our room until 4:00 pm even though we had requested an early check-in for a 1:00 arrival and the hotel sought to charge us an exhorbitant daily rate for a roll away bed for our daughter (which they did agree to waive since we had no notification of these charges) we had a lovely stay.We booked a city view room at got a corner room with a king size bed (ending in 23) with 2 terraces, one overlooking the city and the other overlooking the ocean. The room was clean, bright and sunny and the housekeeping staff was excellent coming early in the morning and coming back promptly if you we were not ready for them. One night my daughter got sick in our bed around midnight and housekeeping was up in 3 minutes to completely replace our bedding (blankets and all) quickly and efficiently. The pool area is nice with a large wading pool for children about 4 years old and younger with a fountain in the middle and the deeper pool with a water slide. The water slide was open 11-4 most days which was ample time for my daughter to go down at least 25 times a day. The pool was not heated and I was very happy my daughter was occupied so I did not have to stand in the freezing water. The hot tub was nice seating about 8-10 people. Like many resorts with tall high-rises all of the chairs in the pool area are in the shade for at least half of the day. There was at least one activity every day for the kids by the towel stand (hula hoop contest or painting ceramics) which was a nice free activity around lunch. My daughter especially liked the cookie decorating around 2 pm.  The beach was very nice. The water was very warm with a nice blue green carribean color. Although the red flag was up at the hotel every day we were there, we were able to wade in a few feet and not be bothered by the waves. The sand on the beach was clean and because of the ample shade you did not have to rent umbrellas (chairs were provided by the hotel for free). The hotel had pails and shovels for the kids to borrow along with some board games.  We only had breakfast in the hotel once and it was your typical large Marriot buffet, it was nice to sit outside in a screened in dining area and look out at the ocean. We usually had breakfast at Danny's down the block who made excellent pancakes and eggs for breakfast and pizza for lunch and dinner. We also enjoyed the Chinese/Japanese restaurant in the hotel which has upscale Chinese food, a sushi bar and hibatchi tables. There is plenty of fast food within walking distance, Starbucks, Haagen Daz and a gelato store (Pia Bella) directly across the street and Dunkin Donuts, Baskin Robbins, Subway and Wendys within 3 blocks. There is a significant homeless problem in the area and it was not unusal to see a half a dozen homeless people sitting on the streets with cups out in front of stores. None of them were intrusive or menacing.  We rented a car one day to drive to El Yunke (the rain forest) and found out that the guided tours there were not offered on Monday or Tuesday but at the information center we were given excellent maps and truly enjoyed driving up to the tower and water falls. It is truly magnificent. On the way back we stopped at a large indoor outlet mall that included stores like Polo, Guess, Nautica and Gap. Overall we had an excellent time and would certainly consider staying here again.

<Author>drTX2
<Content>Great hotel, great location My husband and our two children aged 5 and 6 stayed here for 2 nights before catching a cruise. We thought it was a nice place, probably the nicest in San Juan and liked the location. The taxis in San Juan are fairly safe and easy to work with, they are called Taxi Touristico and have set prices. It was about a 20 min drive from the airport and cost us about $15 to get there. Check in was easy and our room was ready. They offered us a different room in the newer tower for $25 more but we saw our booked room and liked the view and found both to be about the same so we stayed with the original room. The rooms are clean, well-decorated and we had a wonderful view of the ocean from the 19th floor. I am really picky about the bathroom and found that the bathroom was really spotless! Nice toiletries from Bath and Body Works, granite countertops and white tubs without any mold or mildew, and very spacious. The room also had an iron and an umbrella which comes in handy in a place like San Juan. We loved the soft beds and pillows. The maid service was also good and had our room cleaned in a timely manner. We used the pools and jacuzzi which had just been fixed. The pools are a little shady and cool but that was our only option since the waves are rough on the beach. It is a very nice beach to take a walk but would not recommend for swimming with young families. Also the waterslide at the pool is only open at certain times. We heard that Luquillo beach near the rainforest is nice but could not make it there due to the short duration of our trip. We did use the gym at the hotel which was very clean and up to date. They have nice cool towels to wipe down with after your workout and have water and teas to drink. The only downside is you can only use the treadmill for 30 min before it starts to shut down. I think they are programmed this way. We did not have any problems with noise from the lobby or hallways at night. We did not use the casino much as this was not our interest. The weather was gorgeous and we preferred to be out. We did not eat at the hotel because it was overpriced and there are so many options just outside this hotel. Starbucks and Hagen-Daas is right across the street as well as a sandwich shop and a taco chain. Down the street on the right there is Tiajuana's which is a Mexican chain and Danny's International which is a nice italian restaurant with awesome pizza. There are lots more restaurants if you keep walking but we did not need to. Danny's also served up a good breakfast. On the left is Walgreen's which sells everything you might ever need. We brought some cereals from home and just went and bought milk from Walgreen's and put it in the fridge in our room so that we didn't have to run out in case the kids wanted breakfast or a snack. There is also a grocery store in walking distance on the right of the hotel. The bus stop is just outside the hotel and buses are free until Jan. You take C10, B21 or C53 to Old San Juan. From there you catch the green tourist bus or the open trolley bus (still free) and can go through Old San Juan and even to the two forts. Lots of restaurants in Old San Juan and shopping. Near the Sheraton at the pier there are lots of tents with street vendors if you like that type of market. We went to El Morro Fort which is worth seeing. Costs $3 per adult to enter and you can walk through it in about 30 min. It was no problem for the kids to walk through it. Check out from the hotel is at noon. They let us extend to 1 pm which was fine for us because we went to the pier after check out. It cost about $12 and was about 10 min away. We called for the Bellman to take our luggage on the way out but he never showed up so we just walked down with our luggage and saved ourselves $5! The only other problem we had was a charge on our bill for use of Games on the TV which we had to call the front desk to remove THREE times and they finally did on check out. It was not a big problem, just an annoyance because each time we called they said they would take care of it and never did. They do charge you a resort fee of $12 per day but that is just one of the things you have to pay if you stay at this place. Overall, we had a fun couple of days in San Juan and would stay at the Marriott again if we went back. It was relaxing and convenient!

<Author>timezoner
<Content>Nice hotel, but useless concierge We got a great deal directly from the Marriott website (standard ocean front room with brkfst for $223/night plus tax  fees). The room was nice and clean with just enough space to unpack for a week. The resort fee includes 2 bottles of water daily, newspaper, plus towels and chairs for the beach. Some people will find the shower's water pressure a bit lacking. A nice touch is that the bathroom vanity has drawers - reduces clutter. The tub was not draining properly but was promptly fixed. The walls are not thick and you can hear your neighbors. The breakfast buffet at La Vista restaurant is ok, nothing lavish. There is a nice omelet station where you can also ask for fresh scrambled eggs (rather than the ones that have sat out in the buffet line), pancakes, waffles, french toast, etc... The staff is very friendly. The only issue was with the concierge staff. They, too, are friendly and try to be helpful. But they just aren't as good as other hotels. Some of their local restaurant menus are out-of-date by at least a couple years. Good concierges will visit local restaurants and attractions to get experience first hand. It didn't seem like the Marriott's did. There was also a lack of follow up. We asked them to book us for an English tour at Hacienda Buena Vista (a coffee plantation in Ponce). They had a hard time getting the right information from the attraction. Not only were they unsuccessful in booking, they never called us back to let us know status. In the end, we called the plantation directly and took care of it ourselves at the last minute without issues. As comparison, we stopped by El Convento hotel in Old San Juan and asked the concierge for restaurant help. They were more knowledgeable, covered more restaurants, and had current menus, including specials for Thanksgiving Day dinners. On the flip side, they were not friendly (and the poor attitude was worse at their bar). There are two pools, neither is deep. The beach has soft sand but the waves are very strong. The entire week of Thanksgiving was on red flag, ie, go in the water at your own risk. I think of resorts as being more luxurious than this place turned out to be. But overall this is a decent, central place to stay, and I recommend it if you can get a good deal.

<Author>tolland27
<Content>Comfortable and friendly This is a well-maintained property that caters to families, couples and business people. Our king-size bed was comfortable with high-end Marriott bedding -- lots of those special pillows that you can now purchase commercially. Our room was slightly smaller than others -- possibly because of the big bed but was not a problem for the two of us. We paid more for ocean-view and it was well-worth it because we spent a good deal of time on the balcony. The room was well-appointed with pretty art and a large flat screen television. Bathroom was clean although a bit small. Our ac worked but it took time to get the moisture out of the room. I don't fault the system -- this is the Caribbean and I have stayed in other hotels where the ac needs time to get rid of the humidity.My wife and I used the beach where an attendant set up chairs and an umbrella as well as the pool. The pool has a supervised water slide -- great for kids. This was off-season so I cannot comment on the usage. Bar personnel did patrol both the pool and the beach. Staff on this property was helpful and friendly. The hot tub was under repair -- boarded over, so it was difficult to tell if and when it will return to use.Food was hotel-priced but there is a coffee bar in the lobby for light breakfast takeout and a Starbucks and Duncan Donuts across the street. There are take-out alternatives and fast food as well as some very good restaurants along Ashford Avenue. Every three months (we were told), the road is closed down for Friday, Saturday and Sunday evenings for a huge block party. Restaurants brings out tables, and bands -- salsa, jazz, even a mariachi -- play. Quite the scene and a lot of fun. Other amenities: The front lobby has a high noise level as it includes a very large bar and music/dance area. The casino is right off the lobby and was very busy while we were there. There were lots of gambling alternatives -- slots and tables and lessons are offered by the hotel. We also booked a tour to the El Yunque rainforest with a knowledgeable guide. I thought it was good value -- $53 for a 4-5 tour. I have stayed in Miramar, Isla Verde as well as Condado, mostly on business. While Isla Verde has some very nice hotels and is closer to the airport, I found the Candado presented some alternatives to hotel eating that happened to be very good. In all I would certainly recommend this hotel for families, couples, and parents with teens.

Located right in the middle of Condado, In just a short walk you have quite a few places to eat, grab a drink and even a Walgreens. On the weekends the street in front of the hotel shuts down and there are people everywhere with live music, bands and djs elegant and casual its great. Oh and bus stop is right in front of the hotel it was free for us due to elections but in any case its only 50cent a fraction of a cab and really almost as fast to Old San Juan.4. Beach. Well its clean the waters warm and the sand is soft but its a real treacherous place to swim with hard shore pounding waves and lots of body boarders. The beach lounge chairs are comfortable. If you don't like the sand the pool is relaxing and it even has a slide.5. Overall It gets 4 stars because the beach is not the best if your looking for the beach go to Isla Verde its much better but if you want to be near old San Juan but still enjoy the ocean this is a great place right in the middle of it all. FYI: If you are looking to rent a car walk up Ashford Ave a little past the La Concha Hotel to 1050 Ashford Ave Condado, Puerto Rico 00907 call [--]. Amazing service the counter manager really helped us out and gave us a great price about 1/2 of what you would pay at the hotel and took care of our parking ticket too.

<Author>nyuszi
<Content>Great Hotel, but not really a "Resort" This is a great beachside hotel, with all the level of services and amenities you'd expect, but I just wouldn't call it a Resort So, let's start with the good: decent sized room, comfortable beds, nice bathroom with lovely Bath  Body aromatherapy toiletries. They had an efficient front desk staff and good housekeeping. The bad thing about the room was that the AC didn't seem to have the oomph to fully overcome the hot, humid weather, so it was always about 72 F in the room (which was too hot and sticky for fully comfortable sleeping in my book).The beach access was great, though the surf can get a bit rough in the Condado area. The downside is that the beach attendants seem pretty reluctant to help you set up your beach chair and were constantly suggesting that you take other guests' chairs - even if it appears they had just gone into the water rather than left the beach for good. It can also get pretty crowded, but not as bad as you might expect, given the size of the hotel.The Pool area is very pretty and even has a swim-up bar. However, it's pretty family-oriented. The water is no more than 3 ft deep anywhere and there are a LOT of screaming children at all times. So, great if you have children, pretty lousy if you don't. The waterslide is open to adults, though, so you can kind of cross the divide that way.The breakfast buffet is pretty good and definitely a good value. Lunch and dinner options are fairly standard hotel fare. But luckily, there are 3 excellent Puerto Rican/Carribean restaurants within walking distance - Yerba Buena, Ajili Mojili and Vieja Ropa. The casino is small and fun, and they even offer gambling lessons each evening.The location in Condado is really convenient. There's a fair amount of shopping and eating available nearby and you are halfway between the neighborhood of Isla Verde for good nightlife and Old San Juan for cultural/historical sites and good nightlife. Either area is about a 15 USD cab ride away. There is also a city bus that stops on the corner in front of the Marriott and terminates in Old San Juan. It's supposedly 75 cents, but I kept riding for free, and it doesn't appear to follow any kind of set schedule, so I'd only recommend it if you are flexible and like the adventure of riding other city's public transport.All right, so that's all mostly positive, but here's why I really can't call it a Resort. As far as I could see, the only things that differentiated this from a normal beachfront hotel is that they have additional tours and activities available via the Tour Desk and the Ocean Club (aka the Pool). However, these were pretty lame activities, such as cupcake frosting and throwing a volleyball net across the pool. And though the gym facilities were good, the spa was kind of puny. Finally, I have to reiterate the lazy beach attendants. That was really disappointing after spending the first half of the week at a much less expensive location where they practically fell over themselves to be at our service.

<Author>Dragonminder
<Content>Gorgeous Resort Hotel The San Juan Marriott is a beautiful resort hotel in the Condado section of San Juan. It has a stunning bi-level pool and direct access to a broad public beach. Our room was large, clean, and comfortable, and had a widescreen LCD TV -- as well as a wonderful broad shower head with dozens of tiny holes for a wide spread . We had a full view of the pool area and a partial view of the ocean. The hotel staff were all extremely courteous and helpful, and we kept them hopping with many requests, such as for additional towels and glasses.There were 2 minor problems with the room: a burned-out light bulb in one of the lamps -- replaced within 5 minutes after we called to complain -- and a noisy air conditioner vent. We considered moving to another room, but by the second day we were used to the noise and didn't notice it anymore.The hotel has 2 restaurants: La Vista, a casual cafe; and Tuscany, a high-end Italian restaurant. There are several excellent restaurants within an easy walk of the Marriott, and numerous dining choices in OSJ. Food in San Juan tends to be expensive, but it's almost always cheaper to dine outside of the hotel. For a quick, inexpensive breakfast, there's a coffee bar in the hotel lobby, and a Starbucks directly across the street.The bus to Old San Juan stops at the end of the block that the Marriott is on, and takes about 20 minutes to reach Old SJ. The usual bus fare is 75 cents, but all buses were free when we were there. Buses stop running at 10 PM, and a taxi back from OSJ to the Marriott costs about $15.All in all, I would recommend the SJ Marriott - Stellaris to anyone.

<Author>gimmecandynow
<Content>Very friendly and accommodating We arrived at the hotel at 9:00am, and even though check-in is not until 4:00pm, they gave us our room, which was like getting a free day. The room had a large flat screen TV, very comfy bedding, and a very large and updated bathroom. Also noteworthy is that at the time of our stay, the resort allowed guests to decline the 12% daily resort fee. I appreciated this since, like most resort fees, it adds no services that aren't already included in the price of the room.The hotel is within walking distance to many restaurants and shops, and the concierge is happy to give you a list. After eating lunch the first day at the poolbar, we were glad to have the option of going out to eat. Unfortunately, the poolbar food was not good and overpriced, even for a resort poolbar. The beach was well maintained and large, and there is an attendant there to help you with chairs and umbrellas. They chared $12 to rent an umbrella, but there were plenty of shady palm trees to sit under as well. From the beach, you could see that the areas around the hotel were very run down, which detracted from the scene if looking toward the hotel.Overall, we had a very good experience with the Marriott and the staff was extremely friendly, hard working, and accommodating.

<Author>SPAnne
<Content>Great stay! We stayed at the Marriot San Juan Resort and Stellaris Casino for 5 days, and we really had a great experience there!  OVERALL: The room was a good size and it was worth every penny to pay a little extra for the pool/ocean view... it was great to sit out on the balcony with a cold drink and look out at the pool area and (beyond the pool area) the gorgeous clear blue ocean! The room stayed kind of damp/humid all week, but I think some of that may be inevitable given the Caribbean climate! The location was good too. Nice beach, especially if you like playing in the waves (not super calm water, but that was a good thing for us!).  Money-Saving Tip for Drinkers: The drinks at the pool area were definitely overpriced, so we decided to buy our own little bottle of rum and some juice, etc mixers at one of the many little grocery/liquer stores within walking distance. (For about $20 worth of stocking the bar in our room, we were able to get the amount of drinks that would have cost $200 at the bar over the course of the week!).  If you are interested in touring the Bacardi Rum factory, don't book your trip through the tour company in the hotel.... they will likely charge you around $50 per person, and in reality you can get there and have that entire experience for less than $30 total. Overall this was a good afternoon, but we were so glad we hadn't spent $100 to have the tour company take us there! We did book a trip to hike in El Yunque through the tour desk at the hotel, and that turned out to be a very good choice! We never would have been able to pick out the most scenic spot to go hiking had we chosen to rent a car, drive there ourselves, etc... plus it was nice to not have to worry about transportation (it's about 45 mins away).  We ate at the Tuscany restaurant in the hotel one night, and the food was very good. We also managed to find lots of great little restaurants to try within walking distance, and it was fun to just wander around until we saw a place that looked like a good one to try!  Overall, we had a wonderful stay at the Marriot San Juan! Enjoy!

On the way there you are dropped off at a stop on the sidewalk. On the way back you need to catch the bus from the terminal about a block to the west from the stop. (The bus is labeled route 21b). On the way back get off at the stop in front of the Bueno Aries resteraunt (which is directly behind Walgreens). Don't ask me how I know....The casino is small by US standards but it is entirely smoke free. Maybe we will catch up some day.

<Author>Scully1998
<Content>Enjoyed Our Stay! My husband and I stayed at this hotel for 5 days/4 nights. After researching a lot of properties, I chose this one. I am a very picky person so I am always worried about spending a lot of money and not getting what I paid for. This hotel met all of my expectations. Great staff.. everyone said hello and was helpful. We stayed in an oceanfront room on the 15th floor, which was breathtaking (be sure to make sure you are in the main tower and not in the cabana.. especially if you pay for the oceanfront room). The room was very clean, nicely decorated, and had a very private balcony. The bathroom was nice.. but a little small. They offered two pools. One was only 2 ft in depth, and they other was about 4ft. They had a neat water slide that provided entertainment for both kids and adults. I even saw some senior citizens using it.. which I thought was great! They have two pool bars and have happy hours specials. Make sure to get your two-for-one drinks during happy hour. The casino and the live bands were a nice touch. We enjoyed drinks while listening to the music.Some suggestions:1. You can opt-out of the resort fee. We saved about $27 per day by opting out. The only thing we missed was the internet access.. which was great for me b/c I wouldn't be addicted to checking my e-mail for 5 days. Just ask the person checking you in to opt out. You will still get your towle service at the pool.2. If you want to rent a car, rent one through Hertz. They have a counter right in the lobby. We were able to drop the car off in the hotel's parking garage after hours when we were done with the car. It was convienient.3. We chose a room rate that included access to the executive lounge. We had breakfast in the lounge, appetizers, and desserts for three of our days and the food was great. Just be advised that the lounge operates Sunday night through Friday, so if you are coming for the weekend.. don't bother.4. There are great restarants right around the hotel. We had a decent breakfast as well as great pizza (and I am orignially from NY!) at Danny's International restaurant (one block exiting the hotel to the left), a nice dinner (authentic Puerto Rican food) at Ajili Mojili which was about a 15 minute walk to the right of the hotel. We also grabbed lunch from Camille's Cafe and had a nice seafood dinner at Miro, which are directly across the street from the hotel. Just be careful of walking into a sidewalk restaurant. We got sucked into one, and wound up paying $35 for lunch! At least the food was decent. Just check the menu prices.5. If you visit the Rain Forest, don't pay all the money for a guided tour. Once the guy in the visitor center explained the trails to us, it was very easy to follow. The hike down to the bog waterfall is not for your 80 year old grandma, but worth the effort once you get down there. I was upset that I didn't have my swimsuit on. I definitely wanted to jump in with everyone else after our hike down there.6. Try to book excursions on your own instead of going through the hotel. You will save about $20 doing it on your own. We enjoyed the snorkeling catamaran cruise through the East Wind company. They even picked us up at our hotel. That was about 5 hours in length.. with and open bar available for the entire duration. We also went on the bioluminescent kayaking trip. We went at 6:30, which turned out to be great. We could see through the lagoon on the way out and it was dark by the time we got to the area that contained the bioluminescence. The trip back wasn't as fun b/c it was dark and people we crashing into each other. 7. We took the bus into Old San Juan. Although we only paid $0.75 each.. we had no idea where we were once the driver dropped us off. So bring a map. We were very lost and had no idea how to get back. We wound up taking a cab back to the hotel ($14).

<Author>MurphyTXMom
<Content>Great Resort for Family Some hotels in San Juan aren't Family friendly. They tend to cater more to Singles or Honeymooners. The Marriott San Juan Resort  Stellaris is definitely Family friendly. I was there with my 3  6 year olds. They absouletely loved the resort. Their favorite part (and mommy's) was the huge Children's Pool. Usually when I travel, the hotel's Children's Pool is so small you find yourself fighting with other parents to get a spot for your kid. But, this Resort's Children Pool is huge! So Moms/Dads, no worries. The Children's pool is also divided off from the deeper pool, where of course, the older kids and adults hang out. If you're like me, I'm always worried the younger kids will be harmed when the older kids are in the same pool. Again, not a problem here. The resort also has sand buckets, shovels, boardgames etc. for the kids to borrow for free. They're located at the towel hut. They also have books mom and dad can borrow, if you want to lay back and read. It's true that the beach has dangerous waves for young children. But, my kids were content making sand castles and staying on the edge of the water when they wanted to get wet. There is a Starbucks and Hagen Dazz right across the street. And a Dunkin Donuts/Baskin Robbins 2 blocks away. My kids of course loved getting donuts for breakfast and Mom and Dad loved the affordable breakfast. There is also a Wendy's and Chili's not too far away. You can definitely walked there and back (not dangerous).The rooms are beautiful. We stayed in the tower (15th floor) and had the city view. It was just fine for a family. Anyone with kids knows that an Ocean View room is lost on kids. They don't want to see the beach, they want to play on the beach. So save yourselfs some $ and booked the city view rooms that are on the higher floors. Nice view of the city at night. Another nice perk, the local bus is down the block. So with .75cents you can get to downtown San Juan. My kids loved the adventure of riding the local bus. There were many tourist on the bus, so you'll fit right in and feel safe.If its raining out, take a look in your room closet, there's a huge umbrella you can borrow. There's also cozy robes and slippers (for adults) Mom and Dad can slip into later.If you're wondering what the Resort has for Adults? It has Plenty!!. The deeper pool with a Slide, the Swim up bar. The Salsa band each night. The great Bar and Casino and Restaurants. The staff there were so so nice and professional too. That of course is a big plus. You can't go wrong at the Marriott San Juan Resort and Stellaris Casino. We had a great time and hope to stay again during our next visit (hopefully next year).

<Author>LollyMoz
<Content>Great Experience! Stayed three nights 鈥?weekend getaway. Wish we could have stayed longer.鈥?Before arrival called the concierge desk and talked to Nancy who was fantastic. Although she was not able to assist me, she took my contact information in case we were cut off and transferred me to the tour desk where I dealt with Robert 鈥?another wonderful experience. Robert gave me a lot of great information and was extremely helpful. Moments later the phone rang and it was Nancy from concierge making sure I had gotten what I needed. This is before we even got there!鈥?We arrived very early 鈥?11:00 a.m. not expecting our room to be ready. Juan, at the front desk, was able to upgrade us (for a small fee) to an ocean front room on the 12th floor. We went and had lunch and when we came back at 12:30, our room was ready. The bags were delivered within moments of our getting in to the room and the bellman who delivered them was beyond helpful, getting us ice, giving us local area information, etc. We explored the room, which included a small fridge which comes in very handy, full size iron and ironing board, large size umbrella, two wonderful robes and slippers, plenty of good hangers, lots of towels and one bottle of complimentary water (replaced daily). By the way, for the lady who wrote in a previous review that she had such trouble securing a connecting room 鈥?they are available, as ours was a connecting room (1212). The room has a nice balcony with two chairs and a small table. We slept with the door open and the sound of surf putting us to sleep each night. All rooms are non-smoking, so you do have people outdoors smoking on their balcony, which can be annoying if the smell bothers you. The bathroom was really nice with plenty of counter space, four electrical outlets, a deep tub and rainshower-type shower head with good water pressure and plenty of hot water. A particular pet peeve of mine is a toilet that flushes so loud that it wakes up the rest of the floor in the middle of the night 鈥?in this case, the toilet is nice and quiet 鈥?I鈥檓 sure someone out there will appreciate my noting this particular fact! The bed was ultra comfortable as were the pillows 鈥?so much so that I actually ordered a couple of pillows from their on-line store. Cleanliness was top-notch 鈥?the room was spotless. We didn鈥檛 use wi-fi, so can鈥檛 address that issue.鈥?Staff 鈥?as I mentioned earlier, we had a wonderful experience with the staff. There was not one staff member that we encountered during our stay who was not friendly, helpful, and/or smiling. We received a courtesy call the evening of our arrival making sure that we had everything we needed. There are many bell staff opening doors, getting cabs (plenty of cabs readily available at the hotel and they have pre-negotiated rates to various oft-traveled locations, which is really nice).鈥?Pool 鈥?As previously mentioned, this hotel is family-friendly. If you object to kids, then keep this in mind. If, on the other hand, you are looking for a place that has activities designed for children, this is a great option. At the entrance to the pool there is a big activities board that lists all the goings-on for both kids and adults each day. At the towel desk, they also will loan out books and games for all ages. Beach chairs are plentiful, umbrellas do cost extra. Bar staff will wait on you while sitting at the pool and/or beach (the drinks are wonderful, but beware, they will sneak up on you).鈥?Beach 鈥?very rough, yes, but people were still swimming and there are many local young people who surf with boogie boards. The hotel keeps the beach clean. There is plenty of sun to be had on the beach for those who find the pool area too shaded.鈥?Security 鈥?plentiful, both inside the hotel, on the beach (Police on horseback, Police on scooters, Police on bicycles), and in the local area itself. We felt completely safe at all times. We stopped and chatted with one local lieutenant (tiente) who gave us some excellent tips about where to eat off the beaten path, etc. There are panhandlers, as in almost all cities, but they are not as aggressive as I鈥檝e seen elsewhere and the police keep a pretty close eye on them. Primarily they are soliciting change from cars at intersections or outside of shops. 鈥?Misc: Hotel elevators were prompt and high-speed and all in good working order, meaning we never had to wait more than a few moments for an elevator. Lobby bar is definitely the happening spot for dancing at night, offering different themes/styles of music on different evenings. Casino is small, but nice. No smoking in the casino, unlike Vegas. There is a small grocery/liquor store two blocks from the hotel (turn left as you exit the property) and a 24-hour Walgreens (does not sell alcoholic beverages) across the street. There are many restaurants offering any type of food you can think of, within easy walking distance of the hotel. El Dorado, a few blocks away and on a back street, offers a lunch special for $5.50 from 11-3 (you have to ask for it) with everything from chicken to pork chops to seafood and plentiful portions. If you are traveling with young ladies in your group, be aware that there is a tremendous amount of construction going on, and the construction workers are the same as in any other city. They sometimes pay more attention to the sights, than what they are supposed to be constructing. There is very high-end shopping a few blocks to the right as you exit the hotel 鈥?Gucci, Vuitton, Cartier, etc. We went on a catamaran trip with Eastwind Cats - snorkeling trip to Culebra - which was totally wonderful and worth every cent!鈥?All in all, we loved it and will be back. We may stay at La Concha next time 鈥?also a Marriott-owned Renaissance property 鈥?once their construction is done, as it seems they have fewer children and are a touch more upscale (check out their lobby and pool area 鈥?ultra sophisticated.

<Content>Great Beach Hotel in San Juan Our family spent 5 nights at the San Juan Marriott Resort. Immediately I noticed that the staff was very friendly and professional. The hotel and surrounding area have a Miami/South Beach feel. It appears that the local govt. is trying to modernize the Condado area. There is still some construction going on in the area and a few abandoned buildings.The hotel beach is small but nice. As everyone else as stated the red flag was out everyday. There is an undertow but it was manageable. My son is 10yrs old and he had no problem in the water. The waves are perfect for boogie boards and body surfing. In fact seeing local kids boarding was a daily occurence. The sand is soft and the Marriott beach chairs are complimentary. Umbrellas were not. There are two pools, one with a water slide. The pool area is nice but a little small for a large resort. Chairs are at a premium so get down there early. As others noted there is alot of shade arond the pool. However you will have no problem getting a tan.I was a little suprised that there was not a kid's program at the hotel. Although I knew this before we left, once we got there and saw the amount of kids I thought they should of offered one at the property. We have been to other Marriott resorts and they had a Marriott Kids Club. There are organized activities for the kids by the pool daily though.We went snorkling through East Wind and the trip was great. Also a trip to the Rain Forest, El Yungue, is a must. Take the La Mina Falls trail and swim in the waterfall. This was one of the highlights of the trip.The Marriott is a great central location to see San Juan and Puerto Rico. We felt safe in the Condado area. There were cops everywhere and everyone, locals and staff, were very friendly.

<Author>travelduck111
<Content>Stellar! We really enjoyed our stay at the San Juan Marriott after our cruise. The location is absolutely perfect - right on the beach in a great area of San Juan. The rooms are nicely maintained with flat screen televisions and marble bathrooms. There is a nice size casino on premises as well as a lobby lounge with music and full bar. The pool is huge with a wading side and hottub. I especially liked the employees of the hotel. The security staff is all around and very friendly - not at all like the Miami Beach bouncers. The front desk person was also very nice but I could not talk her into a free upgrade. The only negatives I found at the hotel was the guy setting up beach chairs and umbrellas. I nicely asked him to set up an umbrella for my wife and he walked right past her and left the beach with the umbrella laying next to her. Also, the concerge with short black hair was on the phone when I approached the desk. I waited five minutes and she never even acknowleged my presence. Are you ready for some travel duck tips? 1. The hotel has two sections: a main tower and a cabana tower. In my opinion, you want to be in the main tower and insist on a room above the 10th floor. We had a city view room on the 11th floor and could still hear street noise below. Of course, the ocean view rooms are nicer but will come at a cost. I was very happy with the city view room which actually had a nice view of the city. Just don't spend the money for an upgrade and get a pool view room in the cabana tower or a floor lower than 10. The cabana rooms are set farther back from the beach and the lower floors appear to have palm trees blocking some of the rooms. 2. Who likes to spend $18 for a breakfast. If so, enjoy breakfast in the hotel. If you like to spend $3.95 for eggs, bacon, toast, and unlimited good coffee then walk across the street to your left to Piu Bello (the gelato place). When you get there, you can sit outside and enjoy the people passing by. The lunch menu also looked good.3. For an amazing dinner option, walk 15 minutes to your right across the street and go to Ajili M贸jili. The restaurant is fabulous and don't be scared away by the fancy exterior. I found people dressed nicely and very casually in there. The meal was very reasonable - $70 for two people including appetizer, nice tip, 2 entrees, and one drink each. Speaking of appetizer, you must order the sampler platter (1/2 order for two people is more than enough). You can thank me later.4. For lunch options, try Latin Star down the street. - also reasonably priced Puerto Rican food but a more casual setting. Avoid paying $3.25 for water at the hotel by stopping at Walgreens across the street to stock up.5. Enjoy a drink at the lobby bar at night which gets quite lively with the locals. I was there and ending up sitting next to a local who was passed out at the bar in his swimsuit. He woke up and bought these four older ladies from New York some drinks. However, the older ladies refused the drinks and told the nice local to get lost. They went and talked with some guys from New Jersey. I ended up having one of the drinks with the nice local. Okay, why am I telling you this story? Back to the tips :) 6. The beach is beautiful but the surf is extremely rough. Don't let your little ducks go in the water very far.7. A taxi to Old San Juan will cost $12. Don't be ripped off. Better yet, walk to the bus stop and catch the bus for $.75 (exact change needed). While at the bus stop, you will find a few other tourists from the hotel so you can split a cab as another option. 8. I found the streets very safe to walk at night with police everywhere. Of course, use common sense but walking to the above destinations should be perfectly fine. If you want any more TD tips, please feel free to ask!

The room was spacious with a flat screen tv, lounge chair w/ottoman, desk/chair, inroom safe, and one of the best hotel beds we've experienced. The bathroom is also spacious with very nice amenities--robes, slippers, upscale products. We did not bring our laptop, but there is a Business Center where you can use one of the multiple computers to check email and print boarding passes. The Condado Beach area is very nice and safe. There are many restaurants within walking distance, both upscale and casual and lots of shops. There's a Starbucks across the street and a Walgreen's drug store within a few blocks. There were all age groups staying at the hotel with activities for all. Our only complaint/comment would be the resort fee added to the daily room rate. For us it was $19.50 per day and included a daily bottle of water, lounge chair/umbrellas @ beach, room internet access, wireless in public area/pool, free local calls, $5 casino match play coupons. Not sure why this wasn't just include in the regular rate? It's not like we had a choice! That being said, we would still definitely stay there again when visiting San Juan.

<Author>WENEEDAVACA
<Content>Very Clean and Friendly! Very clean and friendly hotel in the middle of the upscale Condado district. Conveniently located near Old San Juan; you must visit El Morro. You can take a bus for just 75 cents each way [busses run inconsistently], or a cab if you prefer. Cheap rental car place called Charlie's across the street is recommended versus the onsite Hertz rental. We drove to the rain forest and Luquillo beach [very close to one another]. Highly recommend for a day trip. Near Hotel there is good selection of shopping and restaurants. If you can't be without your Starbucks, there is one across the street, and a big Walgreens just blocks away for anything you may have forgotten. However I thought the hotel coffee was superior to any Starbucks. Hotel has a casino, or you can go to others nearby. HOTEL staff was VERY polite and helpful at every turn. They really want to please you.The lobby gets quite loud at night because everything is in the lobby area. Food in Condado area is very expensive. Mini frig in room is good for keeping water bottles , juice, snacks, etc... Plenty of convenience store options nearby to stock up on these. Restaurant selection in the neighborhood is good, though we did not have any outstanding meals at any of them. La Concha down the street has good tapas, but again expensive. We had our 2 kids with us, because it was spring break. My younger one had fun, my pre-teen was a bit bored. Nothing really for teens to do at hotel. Pool is small for a hotel of this size -- no deep water for diving, and no swim lanes if that is important to you. 2 Shallow connected pools and water slide make it a good pool environment for families that have YOUNG kids [under 10]. Swim up bar is convenient for lunch. Beware on the weekends [especially holiday/school breaks]-- this place gets swamped with people, making it hard to get pool/beach chairs. They have a club membership for locals to join and use the facilities, and when we arrived Easter weekend, it was a ZOO! Ocean is very rough, so recommend taking day trips to calmer beaches like Luquillo or Isla Verde, particularly if you have kids and/or like longer beach walks. My kids had a blast at Luquillo, and they have lifeguards there as well as bathrooms, food, parking etc... NOTE: Most beaches in PR are public, and many including the hotel do not have lifeguards. There are some unsightly graffitied buildings adjacent to the hotel beach area, and lots of police around for some reason, so if a serene gorgeous tranquil beach is a high priority, this is not the beach for you. I recommend this hotel for people who will venture out, rent a car and take advantage of all the things that the island has to offer -- there is a lot to see and do! However if you are coming for an extended stay and want a place with lots of things to do on the premises and are NOT willing to venture out, then this hotel is limited in its amenities/activities. Also, there is a decent health club [enjoyed using it], complete with staff, and an adjoining spa [didn't use; heard it was okay]. You can keep up with your workout while on vacation. I noticed that many people are out jogging and walking for fitness on the Condado, probably due to its flat terrain. Seemed to be a popular place for business travelers to stay due to convenient location near business districts, and airport. It may seem that I didn't like the hotel, but I did. I just wish that it was less crowded when we arrived on the weekend; during the week it was noticeably less crowded making for a more enjoyable experience. Perhaps during a NON-school break week it would be more relaxing. The weather was beautiful and spring is great in PR, because it is warm without being overly hot. Summer in Puerto Rico can be extremely uncomfortable due to the very strong sun and high temps. No matter what time of year you travel to PR, bring lots of sunblock, and some aloe in case you get burned. Also, hat/visor and sunglasses are a MUST. Have fun and, Welcome to the island of enchantment!

<Author>partyvegas
<Content>Loved the Stellaris in Puerto Rico! I would like to say that the hotel itself was beautiful. We certainly had a beautiful updated room. The carpeting was like new, the room was spacious, very updated with a bigscreen and we had a balcony overlooking the pool and the ocean. Front desk went above and beyond the call of duty and so did the bell service. Our only complaints where that the fine dining restaurant with the buffet said they served until 10:00 but at 9:00 pm they started putting up the food and we where still eating. They never even informed us that they would be doing that or we would have gone somewhere else.We got there at 8:30 and thought we had plenty of time to eat. Also the concierge was not the most helpful. We ended up asking the bartender on the main floor where to go and what to do. His name was Rosendo and he was awesome! After spending $30 one way by taxi to go to Old San Juan for the first two days, we where told by Rosendo that the city bus picks you up just at the end of the first block. It was 75 cents one way. What a difference! You have to have the exact change so go to the casino and get change or the front desk. For the next 3 days we rode the bus. If you go to Old San Juan try and get back before dark since the bus station is kind of dark. I felt pretty safe though, they had police patrolling inside. When you go back to your hotel on the bus they will let you off one block over from your hotel. Just tell the bus driver and he'll let you know when to get off. Usually there are other tourists getting off at the same bus stop. The bus wait is about 15-30 min. NEVER step in front of a bus, they do drive pretty fast. We also went to the Mall of America on the bus. It took about an hour going and coming, but what do you expect for 75 cents? WE got to see a lot of Puerto Rico though, and it was fun.Whew!!! The mall was fantastic! A huge modern mall with lots of neat places to eat and shop. If I went I would start back to the bus stop around 4pm to be sure you get back to the hotel before dark. We ate at the Dragonfly restaurant in Old San Juan which was quite an experience. It is not a place for children. It is a tiny restaurant. Their drinks are awesome, its kind of a party place. They have 2 bars, one in the front and one way, way in the back. We where at the one in the back. It was really fun.The food is Asian and expensive, but really good. The Fort is in Old San Juan. Its about 3 blocks away from where the bus station is. It's on a park. Just look for it you'll see it. It was really very neat and the views from there are gorgeous! Great for pictures. A really delicious place to eat ,is across the street from the hotel. I can't remember the name of it. But you will see the stairs going up to the restaurant and its beside Starbucks. The lobster there was HUGE! My husband was in heaven when he got it. It isn't cheap but well worth it if you love lobster. Enjoy your stay. I would go back again now that I know the system a little bit better. The beaches are gorgeous and the sand is white. The people are so friendly, and will help you.Just picture perfect. Adios all...learn a little spanish there too! :))

<Author>kellygirl67
<Content>Nice Hotel in the Middle of Everything Three friends and I stayed at the San Juan Marriott for three nights (Mar. 6, 2008 through Mar. 9th) as a girl's winter getaway weekend. We arrived for check-in early (around 1:30pm) and were told that they had assigned us rooms but that they weren't ready yet, so they held our bags in a storage area near the front entrance and we were given a claim check to pick up our luggage when we got our room keys. Instead of sitting around the lobby (or pool) to wait for the rooms, we decided to take the tour of the Bacardi Factory ($35.00 to get there by taxi although the tour itself was free) and decided to stop for an early dinner on the way back. We took the ferry from the area near the Bacardi factory (taxi- $3 pp to get from the Bacardi Factory to the ferry and then $.50 for the ferry itself). We ate at La Mallorquina in OSJ and then caught a taxi back to the hotel ($15) so we didn't get back to the hotel till after 6pm at which time our rooms were ready. We got two pool/ocean view rooms w/ double beds on the 11th floor which were clean and very comfortable with a very nice balcony and view. I noticed that our bathroom door squeaked but I fixed it using some lip balm... Our A/C also made a strange clunking sound every time the blower cut off but we quickly got used to it. As other posters have mentioned, the lobby does get loud w/ the local musicians each night, but we couldn't hear it in our rooms at all.... We went downstairs for a drink in the lobby bar and to check out the casino our first night, and noticed that the locals outnumbered the hotel guests 2-1 in the lobby bar and casino (and even more so on Friday and Saturday night) but we weren't treated any differently by anyone (ie. bartenders or casino staff) because we were hotel guests. On Friday we ate breakfast across the street at Starbucks even though they do have a small 'market bakery' food area right in the hotel lobby where you can buy pastries, bagels coffee etc.. then went on an organized tour of El Yunque rainforest and Luquillo Beach. When we got back to the hotel at 5pm we went to the beach but were told exactly at 6pm that the beach was closing (not sure why they close the beach at 6pm each night?) so we moved to the pool area~which says it closes at 7pm although I always saw people in the pool area past 7pm (at least in the hot tub area). As other posters have mentioned, the pool area doesn't get sun until later on in the day and then only for a little while, but I took a quick dip and the water wasn't too cold for me. There were several kids in the pool too although I noticed that the water slide was dry (I hadn't noticed earlier in the day whether it had been working then or not). The air temp. was about 80 degrees every day and the only rain we had the entire trip was late on Saturday evening and it was very brief. After our quick stop at the pool we went to our rooms to change for dinner and ate dinner at the Hotel restaurant Tuscany's (Italian). Everyone enjoyed their meals and afterwards we went upstairs to have a drink in the lobby/bar and listened to the music for a while although it was a little disconcerting because the hotel had a Mexican theme night so they had both a Mexican Marichi group playing and then they alternated that music w/ the local latin salsa/merengue group. We were all tired from our tour so we went to bed around 11:30 pm although I'm sure the party in the lobby lasted until Saturday morning (the casino stays open till 4am). On Saturday we had breakfast in the hotel 'casual dining' restaurant La Vista and although I only had a bagel my friends had the breakfast buffet and said everything tasted pretty good. We went to the beach until noon (there were plenty of chairs and umbrellas available at that time and I always saw several piles of extra chairs so finding a chair was no problem and the hotel staff was very good about moving beach chairs around and setting up umbrellas for guests). I read another post that mentioned the umbrellas cost extra to rent and while we didn't get one ourselves I didn't notice others who did get them paying the staff so I'm not sure whether they're included as part of the resort fee they tack on (approx. $21.00 per night per room) or not? We went to our rooms to change (they had already been cleaned!) and took a taxi into OSJ to go shopping and have a late lunch/early dinner at the Parrot Club. Later on that night, we got a little hungry so we went to La Vista a little before 10pm (I believe they close at 10pm) and the waiter was very accomodating even though they were about to close up for the night, when we said we only wanted to have dessert and coffee. The desserts were all delicious!! On Sunday morning, we went to the beach for a few hours before check-out and then headed up to shower and check-out by noon. After checkout we had a drink in the lobby bar and left to catch a taxi to the airport at 1pm for our flight back home at 4:45pm. We were advised by our taxi driver that the airport got very busy on Sundays so we got there by 1:30pm and while it was busy the USDA Agricultural checkpoint and the TSA security checkpoint lines moved very quickly so we sat around waiting for our flight for about 2.5 hrs. All in all, a very nice trip... Each hotel staff person we encountered were all very friendly and attentive and we would definitely return to the hotel again as it was a perfect area in the middle of everything in San Juan.

We had an ocean view room so we did not see the other buildings while sitting on our deck. It's very true about the rough water. A father and his son had to be pulled out of the water because the waves were forcing them up against the rocks.If you are looking for a clean room, with nice amenities in a central location then this is a great place to stay.

<Author>sci
<Content>Recommend highly My husband and I just returned from a week at the San Juan Marriott. We booked a room with a city view and upon arrival, got upgraded to a corner room, which is always more spacious and in this case, had two balconies to choose from. The room was beautiful and well maintained - great bedding! Every single person we encountered at this hotel (staff) couldn't have been more pleasant or accommodating. Housekeeping, security, concierge, bar, beach hands, towel keepers, casino workers - everyone is obviously so well trained in hospitality. We were impressed. The beach here is small and if you are one to lounge all day, you will have to position yourself way to the left of the hotel in the morning, so that when the sun hits the hotel around noon, you are not caught in the shade. Being on the Atlantic side, the sand is not the usual Caribbean white powder, rather a grainy yellow. Not that this is a problem, just a heads up. Same with the pool area - while lovely, it is shaded by the hotel and trees. The surf can be wild, and the undertow is something to take seriously. You will not find the calm and gentle waves of the Caribbean on this beach. That said, I think it is a positive.The restaurants in Condado are fabulous. We loved Tijuana's close by. The food is authentic and delicious with great service. The La Mama margarita makes it worth the visit and I'll leave it at that! We also found Budatai to be fantastic, very chic. The whole Condado area has changed a great deal since the last time we visited. The shopping is world class - Christian Dior, Cartier, Ferragamo and Miu Miu are a stone's throw away from the Marriott.Old San Juan is not too far, about a two mile walk, and the restaurants there are worth looking into. We went to Marmalade one night and have to say it is one of the finest restaurants we have ever come across. New York style dining, but reasonably priced - at least consistent with other dining in the area.For those that are concerned about safety in San Juan, I will say that we were both very impressed with the level of security. Clearly, this area is growing and the tourism department is going to ensure that visitors are comfortable, and that the area is secure and well maintained. All in all, I can't wait to return to San Juan. I'd return to the Marriott in a heartbeat. If you are a business traveler, don't give it a second thought. You won't be disappointed.

<Author>mschorr
<Content>Recommend this hotel Just returned from a family trip to this hotel. Overall I was very happy with our experience. We traveled with our two children (13 and 11). The gym was serviceable though 1 elliptical machine isn't enough. We had dinner in a few of the local restaurants near the hotel and they were quite good. The negatives were this property is located on a small beach with only about 1/2 mile of beach. Pretty tough to take a long walk on the beach when it's so small. There were no water sports like wave runners or sailboats like other carribean resorts. The water slide was a bit small for my older kids though they enjoyed it. I felt this was more like a hotel with a pool on the beach versus a resort. Clean, nice rooms, eager to please staff, good location.

<Author>SilentSeeker
<Content>Weathering the Storm Just got back from a stay here. Unfortunately the weather was horrid most of the time. Subtropical storm Olga kicked up as soon as I arrived and ruined two days of my stay, and made the next two only tolerable weather wise. It was finally nice when I left. Ha!The hotel is older, but newly renovated. Everything inside is nicely decorated, including some nice holiday arrangements. It was very clean in all areas. There are two restaurants, one casual (La Vista), one slightly more formal ( Tuscany's). The food was good, the service very nice. There was a good lunch buffet at La Vista with excellent dessert. They weren't too pricey either, for a hotel. But they weren't really local cuisine. I ate there mostly when convenient as the weather kept me in at times. There are also several small venues for coffee and sandwiches. There is also a Asian noodle bar in the casino which is pretty good.The casino is decent, there are a couple BlackJack tables, some 3 card poker and Texas Hold'em games that go on. Of course many slot machines are there as well. I didn't get to use the Spa services, but the Fitness center was pretty good, fairly well equipped with modern machines. The room I had was pretty small but very nice. It had a fantastic King sized bed, a nice 32 inch LG Flat screen, and all the typical amenities including Internet access. The balcony was nice and large. Everything was clean and daily cleaning service was prompt and well done. The pool was beautiful, but very shallow. It was more form than function. For some odd reason, the whirlpool was only for use up to 6pm, which is when I believe they turned off the heat. This seems silly, the best time to use the whirlpool is at night. The beach was right off the pool, but only marginal. Scenery wise there are several hotels around that look like they may collapse at any moment and there was construction next door. This hotel is in the city, don't expect a beautiful remote tropical beach. So with that said, the sand and water are nice, no seaweed or rocks, no jellyfish when I was around. The surf is DANGEROUS and UNGUARDED. The red flag was up the entire time. But if you are careful ( adult ) and a good swimmer in shape, the waves can be a blast.Condado is OK, but I would not really bother exploring it much given the Old San Juan is minutes away. Old San Juan is a fantastic old city with much to explore. Great shopping, restaurants, clubs, and history. It is great fun to just walk around it. I would recommend this hotel as a base, Puerto Rico has a ton to do, so I would just use this place as place to relax after exploring the island. Unfortunately for me, I could only do that a couple days. Liked: Service in all aspects, room ( bed, tv, balcony), beach access, pool, lunch buffetDisliked: Condado, beach aesthetics, whirlpool hours

The lobby is huge with a large bar in the center. The casino is off of the lobby. Check in was a breeze however we were there early 1:30 and check in is at 4pm so our room wasn't ready. They had it ready by three however. Our room was neat and clean sort of on the small side for an ocean view room but it was fine for two. THe bathroom was very tiny for a resort hotel but quite fancy with marble top and large tiled bath tub. The food at the hotel in my opinion is limited. Let me explain.Food: Arriving we sat at the lobby bar waiting until our room was ready. There was a small menu scattered on the bar and in leather books on surrounding tables. It listed mostly Japanese/Tai appetizers like Satay Beef, Wonton soup etc. THere were also american meals such as buffalo chicken fingers, a Turkey club ad a few other things. We went to order and the bar attendant said that menu is for after 6pm. It said this no where on the menu. I think he could see our disappointment so he did some asking around and agreed to place our order. The food was fine. We ate at La Vista for lunch one day and had burgers they were fine as well. THe italian restaurant Tuscany had many seafood dishes and very few typical italian dishes Chicken Parm and Fetuchini alfredo were the only basic two I recognized. The items were very expensive. We did not eat there because of this. The hotel has an executive lounge available to elite members I believe. We are Marriott rewards members so we had access. It was the hi-light of the trip. Continental breakfast each morning, H'ordervs from 5:30 -7:30 and deserts from 7:30-9:30 the food here seemed a bit fancier than in La Vista or the bar food we ordered. All the food from the lounged was included in our room price. Pool Area: The pool area seemed nice. We only sat by it one day. It was very windy so we only stayed two hours. Drinks by the pool are not served until around 11am or so. We did not try the drinks. Over all if I had to go back to San Juan for business I would stay there again. No major gripes except for the weather. I do have to say though for a Marriott Resort I really didn't get that Luxury feeling as I have at say the St. Kitts Marriott Resort.

<Author>ERCUR
<Content>Very Nice Hotel Rooms:Rooms were immaculate, just refurbished. Public areas as well were immaculate. Stayed on Pool/Ocean side. If you have rooms on upper floors you can see the ocean, but also see the parking lot next door and construction of other properties going it to the left of the building. Keep in mind that the low-rise rooms are closed and under renovation. This did not present a problem as there was virtually no noise due the renovations . Staff: The staff at this hotel go out of their way to make your stay comfortable with one exception. I saw at least half a dozen waitstaff walking around the pool area in the 4 days there - was never once asked if we wanted anything from the bar. Nancy, the concierge, is especially nice. Very knowledgeable about the city, restauraunts, etc...Beach:Beach area was nice but many cigarette butts in the sand. I think the Isla Verde beach is a bit better. If you want a nice beach without crowds, best to rent a car and go to Luquillo or somewhere outside of the city. Remember, Puerto Rico has 365 beaches, go see them!!! This hotel is not in a 'hotel strip' like Isla Verde. Marriott seemed to be the only major hotel in the area. There is a lot of construction in this area with couple of new high rise hotels/timeshares being built. In a year or two this area of the Condado will be 'hopping' . Dining:Lots of good places close by. Ajilli Mojilli, a traditional Puerto Rican restaurant is a 5 minute walk (try the mofungo with shrimp)! Didn't eat at hotel except for breakfast bar near lobby which was perfect for what we wanted. Very fresh bagels, croissants, etc...I would return to Marriott Stellaris Resort again for a long weekend. Seemed to be a nice all around place for families and singles as well.

There is a bar in the pool or wait service will come to you as you lounge. The pool area also includes some vendors on the weekend. The location is great. You can stroll along Ashford and eat at a variety of restaurants or enjoy the food in the hotel. There is a great deal to do in the area and many convenience stores all within walking distance.There is a full array of tours offered and the concierge service is excellent and well informed. This is the place to be if you like activity. Also a short bus ride to Old San Juan....note: buses have no specific schedule so you might need to wait a bit. Take the bus into Old San Jaun and taxi (which is reasonable) home.The hotel is right on the beach which is spectacular and the beach staff will gladly provide chairs and umbrella (no cost) and serve drinks on the beach. The hotel is very clean and the staff is friendly at all times. This was a perfect vacation and a great property. Don't miss it.

Kudos to them for helping us with the many questions we had and the true service they gave! Seek them out! You can sit out on the balcony while your eating and see almost the entire island. A great view of the sunsets up there too.At the concierge desk at the check in counter, ask for Nancy. She was great in helping out with where to go and what to do. Also, knows alot of history about the island. Great job to her!The local area that it is in at first looks sketchy, but all of Puerto Rico looks like that. Be warned though, there is alot of crime on the Island with the illegal drug trade increasing and alot of gang activity. Hence, why you'll see alot of police all over the place. There are some nice resturants in the area. Stay away from the hotel ones. Very overpriced! Our favorite one was Pure and Natural next to Wendy's. A 5 minute walk from the hotel. An organic cafe that had amazing fresh fruit smoothies and great sanwiches among other fare too.Trips to take - We highly recommend the BioLuminesant Bay at night. This was one of the most amazing things we have ever done. Well worth it! Also went to the El Yunque Rainforest. We booked the trip through the hotel and took the low impact tour which was good. About $65.00 per person all included. Gus was our driver and he made it very enjoyable. He knows every zip code you can imagine too.1st WARNING - Becareful though when booking a trip on East Island Tours which is through the hotel. We booked one going to Culebra which was supposed to be very beautiful. The day of our trip, we're bused almost 1 1/2 hours to the launch spot only to find out they changed the trip because they said the water was too rough. It did not look at all rough. They indicated that they would refund most of the trip which they did not do. Now we are fighting with our credit card company to see what they can do. We recommend that if it is cancelled, do not go because the couple of places they take you to are not worth the trip or money. Be warrned!2nd WARNING - While the hotel is very nice, be warned of the fees they charge you. Our hotel room was $220 night. They charge a resort fee of 10% which nobody could explain to me what it was for. Finally, a manager told me it covered the free internet service (which we did not use), the phone service (which we did not use) and the chairs for the beach (we did use). The last night we were there, I spoke with the mgr and told him that we thought it was excessive to charge us a fee to use beach chairs for what we're charged for the room. He did refund the fee which over a two week period amounted to over $300. Plus, the tax is 11% too. They also sneek in a green tax which again was not explained very well and was taken off the bill. Check your bill out closely the night before you leave and resolve it then, not when you're leaving in the morning. Overall, the good weighed out the bad and we had a good time. But, if your looking for a real tropical vacation, San Juan is not the place. It is a nice place to visit once or twice, but most likely would not go back. The Bio luminescent Bay trip made the vacation worth while.

<Author>LSB_Phila_Pa
<Content>enjoyed the Marriott My husband and I stayed at the Marriott Aug 2-Aug 6, 2007. It was in downtown San Juan, yet a beachfront property. That is an excellent combination. We were in walking distance of most of the restaurants we ate at. The Buenos Ayres Bar and Grill had very tasty Argentinean steak! The Porta Bella italian restaurant was pricey, but you got alot of food for the money. I had the biggest salmon filet that I had ever seen. The lanscaping of all the palm trees in the pool area was very nice. The deepest part of the pool is around four feet. We had a corner oceanview balcony room. One balcony overlooked the pool area and the other balcony looked directly onto the ocean. It was worth the money to book that room. The flat screen tv in the room was a nice size. The bed was very comfortable. The concereiges were great when it came to recommending restaurants. The hotel restaurant was kinda pricey...breakfast costed around $40 (not including tip) for the breakfast buffet for the 2 of us. It was $15 for the taxi ride from the airport to the hotel, which was around a 10-15 minute ride when not in rush hour traffic.The beach was nice; the water was beautiful but is kinda rough. Plenty of people were having a ball jumping the waves or riding boogey boards on the waves. Its definitely more for that kind of stuff as opposed to swimming. The gym was kinda small but we did get in a decent workout with weights and cardio. The cardio machines have flat screen tvs attached to them. The only negative thing is that the walls seem kinda thin. One room next door had kids. Maybe the kids were kinda loud, but there were times when we could hear their conversations...not enough to wake us however.When we checked out I left my cell phone charger in the room by accident. I realized it after we got back home. It took a couple of phone calls to find out if they had it. They did and hotel did send it back via DHL at their expense.We would indeed go back.

<Author>LongIslandMom3girls
<Content>Loved the Marriott We traveled to this hotel at the end of July. We traveled with my family of five and my parents. When we booked, they would only allow 4 in a room, so one of my kids stayed in my parents room. As it turned out we had five in my room, and nobody cared. I requested a crib when I booked, again at check-in, but had to call down for one again in the evening. It was delivered promptly. They also charge taxes that I was unaware of-a daily resort fee and an occ. fee that was $5 a person per day. There was no shuttle from the airport, but getting a taxi was easy and not too expensive.With that said, the hotel was undergoing renovations, but it did not affect our stay at all. We had 2 oceanfront rooms for 6 nights. The rooms were recently renovated-so they were updated and clean! The staff was helpful and friendly. There were plenty of other kids and activities to keep mine busy. The pool pump broke one day for about 6 hours, but they compensated by serving free pina coladas and rum punches all day-we just went to the beach instead. The casino was small and crowded towards the weekend, but a few short blocks away was a larger casino in the Radisson. We also found some great restaurants within walking distance. A taxi ride to Old San Juan cost us about $12.We would definitely book this hotel again-location was good (no airplanes), staff was friendly, and the hotel had everything my family needed.

<Author>superfig
<Content>Relaxing Vacation The Mariott resort was very nice and their outside pool area and beach was very peaceful and relaxing. We didn't have any issues with cleanliness or noise. The only thing that was annoying were the elevators ...even though there were four of them, we waited quite some time for them. We stayed in one of the renovated rooms and were very pleased. Our balcony was on the side of the hotel, but we could still see the ocean from our balcony. I wouldn't have paid additional money per night to have a better view, but that's a personal choice. Because my boyfriend has Platinum status with Mariott, we were able to us the Preferred Guest Area on the top floor - if you are able to get access to this room, I would recommend doing it. They had a complimentary full breakfast (so we never had to go out) and at night they had coffee, deserts, and appetizers. The view from this Suite was quite beautiful.I wouldn't reccomend eating at any of the restaurants in the hotel...however, the Pool Bar/restaurant was good for lunch without having to leave the pool area.There are tons of great restaurants within blocks of the resort: my favorites was Dannys for Italian food, Tijuanas for Mexican (take a left out of the hotel for these 2) and for some excellent Puerto Rican/Cuban food we walked 8 blocks through Condado past the Designer boutiques to Ropa Viejo (take a right out of the hotel)...it was excellent! Cherry Blossom was the Japanese Sushi and Grill restaurant next door - it was good, but no different than the same restaurants in the States...By the way, Mojitos were excellent everywhere we went!

<Author>travelsavvypr
<Content>Friendly Staff, Good Family Hotel The San Juan Marriott Resort is located in the Condado area of San Juan. It is right on the ocean with a little patch of beach. It's not the prettiest beach on the island but it's nice for laying out and cooling off. The staff was one of the friendliest I've encountered. They were very helpful. Walking down the hall, they would greet you and smile sincerely. The rooms were clean and the balconies were a nice bonus. The pool area is definitely oriented towards families and is filled with children. If you are looking for a quiet, serene pool scene this hotel isn't for you. They had a nice Italian restaurant in the hotel that I would recommend, if you don't want to leave the property. It's about a $10-15 cab ride to Old San Juan for those interested. I wouldn't suggest this hotel for couples looking for romance, but if you have a family or just need to spend a night before or after a cruise this is a perfect hotel for you.

<Author>shirleykr
<Content>Pure Luxury My family just returned from 5 days at the San Juan Marriott. I cannot say enough about this fantastic hotel. We were treated like royalty the entire time we were there. The hotel was beautiful and the staff was very professional and friendly. Every part of the hotel was extremely clean as well as our room. We had an ocean view room with a balcony. The beds were very comfortable, the bathroom was large with marble counters,and my children enjoyed the plasma TV. Anything I requested, (wake-up calls, extra towels, extra pillows) were provided to me right away. We spent a lot of time at the 2 pools. My husband and I tanned while our 2 teenagers played vollyball in the pool.The pools are clean and refreshing, towels are provided,and the pools are open until 11:00 p.m. The ocean behind the hotel is great if you like big waves. I am not much of a swimmer, so I could not handle the big waves, however the rest of my family enjoyed the big waves washing over them. The staff put out beach chairs in the morning for the guests to use all day, hearing the waves crashing up onto the shore was very relaxing. There is a Wendys, Subway, Burger King, Baskin Robbins, Dunkin Donuts, and a Walgreens, all within a few minutes walking distance away. We went to El Morro one day, I suggest you take a cab if you want to go. We tried taking the bus, we had to transfer twice, ended up taking the wrong bus, and then missed our stop. The weather was beautiful, even though its hot, there is a constant breeze blowing that keeps you comfortable. We like to go to a different place each year for vacation, however if we ever visit San Juan again, we will, without adoubt, stay at this hotel again, we loved it!
