<Author>crackofdawn
<Content>3 Pleasant Days We stayed for 3 days in July, 07. Had a ocean facing room (as all are on the older, shorter 9-story building). 3rd floor room so we had some palm tree shade in the morning making the balcony a bit more enjoyable. If you want and unshaded ocean view, probably need to be on floors 6-9 or on the North, East, or South face of the towers (west face overlooks city view in the Tower section.) The older building is plagued with two very slow elevators so be prepared for some extended delays or to using the stairs (our choice). We had a rental car for 1-day ($14 do it yourself parking at Marriott) and cab fare back to the airport for 2 with 4 suitcases was about $20 or so.The lobby can get really noisy as it is a large bar with live entertainment on some nights (Sat night was really full, loud, and lively) -- with a 2 drink min. as well. The casino crowd adds to the activity. The casino is on the south side of the lobby area and is quite a bit larger than it was 5 years ago.We skipped the pricey meals at the Marriott and did the following: for lunch we went to either Subway, Wendy's or BK all of which are within 5 blocks either way on Ashford. Returning to our balcony with a bottle of wine from the nearby grocery store (3 blocks south of the Marriott). Usually skipped breakfast. For dinner: number one recommendation is Pamela's in Ocean Park (about 2-3 miles south of the Marriott on Ashford). This is one great restaurant. It is small and is part of a boutique hotel on the beach. They have superb service and excellent menu choices (creative Nuevo-Latino offerings). 8 tables are set up in the sand, under the stars with candlelight and they have maybe 10 -12 tables inside. Since Ocean Park is a gated community, you enter the guard station on Santa Anna and drive to the water where you'll find Pamela's.We also ate at Yerba Buena which is on the west side of Ashford and 1 block south of the Marriott. Enjoyable PR food, excellent service and innovative drinks. A 3rd night we ventured north of the Marriott on Ashford to AJILI-M脫JILI. Would not go there again. Though it was very busy, we found the service very slow compared to the other restaurants, a miserable 1-page wine list (no kidding!) and unimaginative menu choices. Should have gotten a cab and returned to Pamela's!

<Author>bigzipz
<Content>Loved the Marriott in San Juan My wife and I and another couple just returned from a week at the Marriott Resort in San Juan. Our friends booked hotel and flight thru a travel agent, we booked directly with the Marriott website and used award points for the airfare. The wife and I had no trouble at check in, getting exactly what we'd expected. The friends were delayed getting their room, being told it would be just a few minutes. Two hours later, they were given an upgraded room with executive club privledges with an apololgy. When they went to the room, it was already occupied. they were moved and a little while later, another couple was given the same room. After the initial logistical problems were worked out, the remainder of the stay was uneventful.Pros: The staff at the Marriott is amazing. All - the front desk, the housekeeping, bar and beach attendants - were very courteous, helpful and there to do anything possible to make the stay enjoyable. The Conceirge staff is spotty, with the experienced folks (few) very knowledgable and helpful and the younger folks (many) helpful but not having the experience to really have any value-add. The grounds are spotless and people are always working relentlessly to keep them so. The beach is beautiful and the soft sandy bottom extends out farther than you can stand. The rooms were spacious and clean, very quiet and the A/C worked great! The Tuscany Restaurant on the ground level is one of the best Italian restaurants in San Juan - be sure to ask to be seated at a table served by Alfredo. Great health club! Leave your laptop at home, you get one hour per day of PC/Internet time in the business center per day. Cabs are cheap, figure on $12 to go just about anywhere.Cons: Food and drinks are abundant but not cheap. Average drink price is $8-10 and plan to spend ~$150 per couple on dinner with a fair bottle ($45) of wine and around $45 per couple on lunch with a beverage each.The hotel is located in town and there's a lot of construction going on around it. Some of the buildings look like they're ready to fall down and they do detract from the experience. It does look like they're trying hard to refurbish the area. Overall, it was a great vacation. We probably won't do it again but only because we'll continue to explore the islands for new and different experiences.

<Author>kjscap
<Content>Not our scene My husband and I ended our Puerto Rico trip with three nights at this property. We had a rough time at check-in. We arrived a bit after four, which is check-in time and waited in a very long line to be told there were no rooms ready for us at that time. We were given a restaurant type pager and told to wait. We ended up wandering around a bit and having a drink at the pool bar. I really feel that Marriott should have done something for us, like comped a drink while we waited or something. We also went to speak to the concierage. Her name was Glendaly, I believe, and she was wonderful. After nearly two hours I went to inquire about getting a room and she helped us to finally get checked in. Our room was oceanfront in the remodeled tower and was fine. We were on the 6th floor and could definitely hear the lobby music until two am every night. It may be better to go higher. The elevators take FOREVER though. After check in we walked down the street and ate at an open air trattoria. The streets were very crowded and seemed safe enough to us, even after 10 pm. There was a prom at the hotel that night, and of course that was a bit annoying.The pool is small. It looks big on the hotel website, but it is tiny and totally over run with kids. There are apparently no rules prohibiting float toys so I was run over by a shamu thing that took up half the pool several times. Also, there are a lot of chairs, but many are in the shade and are lined up four rows deep. So unless you want to lay out packed like a sardine you do have to get down before noon to get a good spot. I really was not a fan of the environment down there. Tons of kids and kind of trashy people. The beach was nice. We took cabs to San Juan after being told NOT to take the bus since it has no real set schedule. The cabs were reasonable. The casino is jam packed with old locals at night. It was actually hard to move in there or get to play. We won a little bit. The lobby is packed at night. I have never seen a hotel bar so crowded. All in all I would look elsewhere if I had it to do over. The rooms were fine for our purpose, but it really seemed like more of a city hotel than a resort property, and the kids and type of people that seemed to be staying there made me uncomfortable. I would look at the Hilton maybe since it was closer to old San Juan.

<Author>Betweet
<Content>Nice hotel, Nice pool, Nice beach Went to San Juan for vacation, picked the Marriott because of the location, pool and beach. Overall I loved the hotel, it's not a 5 star hotel but it met all our expectations. The staff was all friendly, went out of their way to say hi and met our needs. I don't recommend eating at the hotel unless you don't mind paying lots of money for a meal..... easily 18-24 dollars for each person. The restraunts surrounding the hotel are just as expensive. The walgreens was nice to have close bye but don't buy the milk... close to being sour. In previous reviews people recommended taking the bus to old san juan, very cheap 75 cents, if you dont mind waiting 30 minutes and driving through rough parts of the town. We were told we could just catch the B21 to get back to the hotel.. what a nightmare, no signs telling you which way they are going, no brochers explaning the process. Lucky us caught the bus (going the wrong direction) took us 3 blocks back to the bus terminal (which is a scary place to sit and wait for a bus) and told us to get out. Didn't know that you had to go sit down 20 feet ahead and let the bus driver take a 20 minute break and then get back on the bus. Helpful hint, spend a couple of extra dollars and take a cab. Over-all the good out weighed the bad and we had a good time. If your looking for a tropical vacation San Juan is not the place. It's a nice place to visit but most likely wouldn't go back. The rain forest and snorkel adventure made the whole vacation worth while.

<Content>Absolutely loved the San Juan Marriott! I rated this above average hotel a rating of EXCELLENT on the overall experience. My husband and I, along with several of our friends had a wonderful stay in San Juan. While I went to great extents to research exactly where we would stay, I had my fingers crossed and I prayed that my selection was a good one. I was pleasantly surpised to see that most of the reviews I had read on Trip Advisor were accurate. The renovated corner rooms in the tower section of the hotel are absolutely beautiful. You have two balconies, once which is ocean front and the other is either ocean or pool view. Beware of the cabana rooms as most of those are not renovated and the difference between the two (renovated and non-renovated) are like staying at the Waldorf Astoria versus Motel 6. Great pool...you even get some eye candy (pool boys) passing around fruit while you take in some rays. Excellent beach front property overall.The location of the hotel, in Condado, is ideal; close to high-end shopping (Gucci, Louis Vuitton, Cartier to name a few) are walking distance. There are also a few non-national brand boutiques that have a great selection of fashion. There is no need for a rental car, taxis are readily accesible. Old San Juan is great and is only a 12-15 minute drive from the hotel. A lot of national brand shopping mixed with other quaint boutiques. Plan to spend a day or two in Old San Juan to get everything in. El Yunque (the rainforest) is also a MUST. The drive is long, so booking through the hotel is a safe way to go - $64 (includes transportation and tour of the forest).The Barcardi tour, in my opinion, was very boring. The taxi ride from the hotel was $35 plus $5 for each additional person, $36 wait time (if you want the taxi to wait while you take the 1 hour tour) and the same price for your return. Needless to say, you are paying for the free tour in the taxi fare. However, the two free drinks and the Barcardi store are a nice compliment to the otherwise boring experience.Night life at the hotel is always jumping, but be sure to venture out to Club Babylon and some other local spots to get a true feel of Puerto Rico. Lastly, the hotel food is somewhat expensive (to be expected). So take time to venture out to some of the local restaurants in Old San Juan. There are too many to name, but just ask a few of the friendly locals or hotel staff. They were very helpful to us in finding great spots to go for a nice meal.I would definitely visit again and stay at the San Juan Marriott.

<Author>costarica99
<Content>Nice urban oasis Stayed at this resort for 5 nights mostly for business. Overall, the hotel was excellent, especially considering that I stayed there during the busy Memorial Day weekend. Pros:Rooms: Very good. Stayed in the tower. Be sure to ask for an upgraded room in the tower. Room had flat screen TV, bathrobe, comp bottle of water each day. Ocean or City View options were available. Food: Had a nice pool side lunch. Pool service was prompt. Very nice coffee bar handy for breakfast take-out to the beach. Staff: Very courteous! Concierge was very helpful. Complaints were handled promptly. Parking: I suggest valet parking. It didn't cost much more than the garage and the staff was prompt. Location: Very convenient. Starbucks, Walgreens across the street. Old San Juan, where most of the action is, is about 3 miles (see below) Very close to the airport. Beach access is excellent. Beach: Beach service was great, with attendant ready to set up your umbrella and chair. Of course, bring a few dollars to tip the guy. Ocean is fun, but can be a little rough for the kids. Ocean water is what you might expect, refreshing, but you are swimming next to a major, urban location! Restaurants: In the neighborhood, there is an adequate, pricey, sushi place next door. Old San Juan: Definately go to Dragonfly, Agua Viva and Parrot Club. For a great local sushi option, don't miss Jinyas, it's a drive, but worth it!Health Club: Top notch. In the basement of the old wing, this place has all of the equipment you'll need. They also provide one comp bottle of water to guests who work out. Safety: I noticed plenty of staff around, both at the pool and beach areas. While there does appear to be a high crime rate, like many urban areas, the hotel and surrounding areas felt safe to me. Jogging: Suggest an early wake-up and do the three mile (each way) jog to Old San Juan. Other: At the concierge desk, there are handy maps to most of the tourist locations with easy to follow directions from the hotel. Cons:Rooms: Be sure to stay away from the ice machine/staff entrance elevator. It tended to be noisy. A squeaky staff door was repaired promptly after I complained. Broadband: Since I was there for business, I had to use the wireless service. In the room, this service was HORRIBLE. I complained but there was absolutely nothing they could do to speed it up. There is a business center with faster service. Location: Taxis are not cheap. It was about a $12 cab ride to Old San Juan. Pool: While there are plenty of beach chairs, the pool is awkward. A huge wading pool and rather small regular pool. Probably great for kids, but not so nice for most folks. Restaurants: Avoid the gelato place down the street. It just didn't taste very fresh!! Rates: Be sure to have them explain their resort fee. This is not a problem, but it is almost automatically included on your bill. Check in: Could have been much faster. The hotel promotes express check in, but I couldn't find it. Casino: Well, maybe because I lost money. It just wasn't a pleasant place to spend the evening. Elevators: Slow, but I did stay over the busy holiday weekend.

<Author>KevinandMichelle10
<Content>Everything we wanted for our Honeymoon The Hotel staff was incredibly friendly and welcoming. They really made it seem a pleasure to serve us. We had an oceanfront view room that was beautiful. The beds were very comfy and falling asleep to the sound of the ocean was nice. We were a little disappointed that the swimup bar and the beach bar closed so early. The beach bar is only open until 7. The concierge was very helpful and saved us a lot of money by suggesting renting a car instead of taking a tour to the rainforest. I really can't understate how the friendliness of the staff made our stay enjoyable. As far as eating, we ate at the Cherry Blossom right next door, which is a Japanese restaurant where they cook the food right in front of you. It's very good but expensive. We also ate at Yerbe Buena(right across from Dannys) which has very good food. We ate at Dannys every day for their breakfast. Their fried egg sandwhich on a hoagie is phenomenal. There's also a place called The Burger Joint which has one of the best hamburgers we've ever had. Take a right out of the Marriot and it's only a few blocks down on your left. We got a little tired of Puerto Rican food so this place was great.The Rainforest was nice. I recommend going to the top trail with the tower. The view is spectacular. Note, when you get to the top of the first part, look for the sign that says Wildlife Viewing Area and take that trail to the tower. The other road doesn't lead to much of a view.We also went to Old San Juan and it was a lot of fun. There's a really beautiful walk that goes right by the ocean around the city. We went on the Bacardi tour which we both thought was a waste of time. It's basically two hours between travel and everything else to get two free drinks each. The rest is a big commercial for Bacardi.The location of the Marriot is great. Starbucks is right across the street and there's a Walgreens a block down for anything else you might need. If you want to find beer or wine, take a right out of the Marriot and there's a store on the left side down a few blocks which had the cheapest and widest selection. We heard a lot about how it's dangerous in Puerto Rico but we never had any problems or felt unsafe. The people there are extremely friendly and offer great advice(such as, 30 SPF suntan lotion isn't going to cut it.)Between the weather, food, staff, room, and view we had a great time and can't wait to go back.

She verified that I needed it in the morning, and ran away with it. By the time I got back from dinner at La Vista (8:00p?), the blazer was already back in my closet, with all- ALL of the cuff buttons clearly removed and resewn, and no more jingling! Then, promptly at 7am the next morning, Peggy called to verify that I had the jacket, and that everything was done- WOW. I asked who I needed to pay, and she said there鈥檇 be no charge鈥?her comment: 鈥渨e want you to look good for your meeting.鈥?Very, very, very nice.I don鈥檛 gamble, so I can only judge the casino from one walk-through. It seemed to have sufficient blinking lights and card tables to make the folks there happy. Can鈥檛 speak to anything else there.One plus was the proximity of Starbucks (at least for me鈥?. It鈥檚 directly across the street, less than 25 yards from the front door. If you鈥檙e in town for business, and can鈥檛 wait for room service at 7am, or the lobby coffee place to open, Starbucks doors unlock at 6am, and they鈥檙e closer than walking to the beach. Also, there is a full Walgreen鈥檚, with grocery section, less than 100 feet down the street鈥?again, easy and safe to get to.The Marriott鈥檚 beach might have been a disappointment鈥?had I been here for vacation. This is not a clean, green, palm tree-lined beach鈥?we鈥檙e in the midst of the Condado area鈥?think Ft. Lauderdale or Miami, not Magen's Bay, Laguna Phuket, St. John, Marco or Hilton Head. It鈥檚 high-rises, right up to the waterfront. If you want remote, quiet, trees, desolate beach, this ain鈥檛 it. Also, there鈥檚 apparently a vicious undertow here, so be careful. I ate at three restaurants at the Marriott鈥?La Vista is their generic Marriott restaurant, which had a regular menu and good wine selections, although not overwhelmingly great. An order of calamari arrived ice-cold from the kitchen, but a smile and a quiet word had it whisked away and quickly replaced with a correctly hot dish and an apology. Also ate at the Italian restaurant, which had a gracious Italian wine list, and a good menu. Very tasty, but seemed quite expensive.Finally, ate at the pool bar/grill before my flight out. Everything served with plastic, but the grilled chicken sandwich was certainly good. Waitress was attentive and helpful. Again, a bit expensive, but no complaints.There seems to be live entertainment in the lobby area each evening, of varying grades of quality. The lobby itself may be one of the largest lobby bars in all of Marriottdom, the casino is to your right, bar is directly in front of you, and the front desk, almost an afterthought, is to the far left. Enormous bar, serving 7x24... heck, there were folks sitting at the bar drinking at 6am when I was heading over to Starbucks! That said, if you want to walk off a plane, into a lobby, and into a cool drink, though鈥?this is the place. Reminds me a bit of the Marriott Frenchman鈥檚 Reef or Marriott Bal Harbour鈥?but it鈥檚 a resort hotel, right?There was hi-speed wifi in the room, which was certainly serviceable. The plug array under the flat-screen tv was helpful, and I never once crawled on the floor to get cables connected. Did not visit the business center, so can鈥檛 speak to that.One bugaboo (and I see this at too many Marriott鈥檚) is the outsourcing and abdication of responsibility for postage. I wrote a postcard to my daughter and my Dad, and then needed stamps. The front desk sent me to the gift shop鈥?who insisted I needed a 39c stamp, and then charged me 46c per stamp. New postal rates: 26c for a postcard. Let鈥檚 be clear here: Marriott has allowed their gift shop to charge a highly visible 77% markup for a blinking stamp. This is really poor, and Marriott should be embarrassed at this.Overall, though, a very, very good hotel. Hardware and software worked well together. Room was clean and very comfy. Employees helpful and service oriented. For me, in town for business, I was delighted. The room was just terrific, services were solid, and internet access worked well. Food was good. Giftshop (expensive stamps and $3.55 Wall Street Journals) was very poor.I would not, though, book this as a week-at-the-beach vacation, purely because the beach was surrounded by high-rises鈥?I鈥檇 be looking for something a little more, well, beachy. For business visits, or one-night pre or post-cruise, I鈥檇 be very much in favor of this property.

<Author>queenbuc
<Content>Beautiful hotel Just came back from an all girls trip to Puerto Rico. We originally booked the Caribe Hilton with the expectations of a nice hotel. The lobby was beautiful but after seeing the room we quickly exited stage left. Definitely not worth the money!!So we headed over to the Marriott. It was beautiful. The lobby was nice. The bell men were cute and the rooms were clean and nicely decorated. Our first room had some leakage problems and we were promptly relocated (with help) and given a $100 credit. We didn鈥檛 eat at the hotel at all, too pricey for us. There is a great restaurant down the street with really good Puerto Rican food that is open 24 hours. I can鈥檛 remember the name of it but it is right next to Walgreen鈥檚 on the Ashford Ave. side. The portions are large so we either shared or took the leftovers back to the hotel. We inquired about a microwave and a few minutes later a guy was knocking on the door with a microwave to put in the room, free of charge!!After realizing all the taxi rides were going to cost a small fortune, we chose the bus. Only $.75 each way! The bus goes everywhere from Old San Juan to Isle Verde and even the airport. Old San Juan is nice and perfect for tourists. We found a little shack by the port that served the best Marlin pastelillos, the manager, Andres is really nice. We also caught the ferry over to the Bacardi plant for free drinks!!! The souvenir shops definitely weren鈥檛 as cheap as the Bahamas. The clubs were okay. Too many young people though. Senior Frogs has a great atmosphere but leaves something to be desired in the food department. We decided we wanted to get away from the tourist spots and wanted to rent a car. The Hertz desk at the hotel wanted $40 a day!!! So I went down to the business center which is open 24 hours a day and booked a small compact car using Hotwire for $12.95 a day. The total for the day was less than $20. The only bad thing is the $14 parking fee at the hotel is ridiculous!!! We rode the bus to the airport, picked up the car, and hit the highway. There are small tolls as you drive up the highway, the most expensive one was $1.50. We drove up to the El Yunque rainforest, which was only a 45 minute drive. The tours from area hotels range from $40-$50. So we were expecting an entrance fee of some sort. Well to our surprise it was completely FREE. We walked the trail to the La Mina waterfall. We didn鈥檛 go to the peak this time, we heard it was beautiful. Either way, you can鈥檛 beat this FREE excursion.All in all we had a great trip to Puerto Rico. I would stay at the Marriott again, however, I would rather rent a condo off the beach.

There are tours from the hotel, we did the rain forest with the waterfall- just beautiful.The pool was nice and there were plenty of chairs around. The beach was ok, waves were strong and it was a city beach (obviously) so it was not as pristine as in other parts of PR. <Content>Pricey for a ghetto resort We stayed at the San Juan Marriott Resort and Stellaris Casino for one night on our way to the Dominican Republic for spring break. Cab fare to the hotel for 4 of us with 4 suitcases and a golf bag was $18.50USD.The hotel has a tall tower, maybe 20 floors, and then a 4-5 floor high wing (the cabana rooms). We requested a low floor in the tower because we had heard that the tower rooms had been renovated already but the cabana rooms had not. We were put in a tower room on the 18th floor, overlooking the pool and the ocean. The room was nicely decorated and clean, and had a new flat screen tv.The beach in this area has tan/brown sand. The water is bright blue/green. The pool at the resort is very nice and has a little water slide and swim up bar. They are obviously trying very hard to be a resort. The problem is that the area surrounding the hotel beachfront is all either graffitied and run-down, or under construction. Maybe eventually it will get cleaned up but we were really not enticed to walk along the beach, for example.This does not stop them from having resort prices. Our room was about $400 for the night (+/- tax) for a single room with two double beds. Hamburgers at the pool grill were $12, a bottle of corona was $5. The Vista restaurant in the hotel offered a lunch buffet for $22 per person and a breakfast buffet for $17. We did not do either and didn't even check the dinner prices.Out on the street side of the hotel you are within easy walking distance of a starbucks, walgreens, dunkin donuts, wendy's, and subway - in addition to several little local joints. We would only stay here again if we were on our way to somewhere else and this was a stopover for one night. This is not somewhere I'd want to go for my entire vacation.

<Author>fellow-in-chelsea
<Content>B++ : quibbles here and there  In the interest of disclosure: Moderate-price traveler. 10 night stay. Pool  Ocean view, non-renovated, non-smoking room. Instant review made during day six of 11 day stay. Gastronome and oenophile.  Overall good-to-great review. Hotel is WELL-LOCATED in Condado district of San Juan. View from balcony of our room was spectacular. Surf was audible all day and night -- which i find pleasant. Hotel's decor is not swank but not homely either. Situated on the beach with a Walgreens, bodega, bus stop and several reataruants within a minute's walk. 2 pools. Beach chair and umbrellas available. During my stay about 65%-plus of the persons at the Hotel appeared to be families with children. A few straight couples. Almost no GAY/LESBIAN persons (sadly) seemed to be present.Beds are comfortable. Linens are soft. Staff is friendly and accommodating. For example: myself and companion often used the Privacy Please sign and the maids would ask when or if we would like the room tidied. Concierge is helpful. The quibbles: Rooms could use renovation, in particular the carpet. CD player in room would have been nice as would have been a better television (I did not use the television). In-hotel restaurants are fair at best. The Italian restaurant, is particularly mediocre given its $20+ entrees. Stick with the more casual dining option (La Vista). Wine choices both by the bottle and by the glass at the hotel are horrendous. Condado and Old San Juan are to my taste clearly not gastronomic or oenophile destinations. No vegetable other than root vegetables (plantains, cassava, yucca) could be found in the local restaurant offerings. Migas (dinner), while exhibiting a beautiful modern decor (and stunning marble or alabaster bar lit from below), presented sculptural but uninspiring food -- salt seemed to tb the preferred flavoring. Migas does have a varied wine list that is superb as compared against Zabo, Aguaviva, and Buena Yerba. My worst food experience to the date of this entry was lunch at Buenos Ayres on Condado ave/st(?): I sent back the soggy fried calamari; the coconut shrimp was encased in coconut such that no shrimp could be tasted; the house salad was all boston lettuce and unripe tomatoes.Hope this is helpful.

<Author>MimiCSeattle
<Content>Pretty Good But Could Be Better I recently attended a week-long conference at this Marriott and from previous reviews knew to ask for one of the remodeled rooms. I really recommend this because my colleagues' rooms were terribly shabby, but the new ones are very nicely appointed, if a bit on the small side. I also had a corner room which had a gorgeous view of the pool, beach and city (at an additional cost of course). I enjoyed my stay until day four when construction started around 8:00am in a room near mine. The noise was like a small jack hammer that could not be escaped, even with earplugs. I politely asked to move rooms but was told there were a lot of people coming in that day and to check back later in the day. The situation was handled very poorly and I am following up for partial credit on the room because they never moved me and construction started early the next morning. Besides this pretty major glitch, the rest of the experience was nice: pretty public areas, great pool and beach. One thing that you should note when reserving is that the price of the hotel does not include a $25 tax + $22 resort fee. We were part of a group so it was not clear whether this was to be expected but that seems like a significant addition on top of an already high room rate if you're not expecting it. The hotel is a $12. cab ride away from Old San Juan, which is postcard beautiful and has some really great restuarants. We enjoyed several including Baru which had great food (sit outside) and Amadeus, which had a great ambiance with live Spanish music and a great menu that includes excellent seafood. I also suggest starting off your night at the upstairs bar at El Convento (beautiful little hotel) and a post-dinner walk on Paseo de la Princesa. PR is beautiful and the people were extremely warm. It's impossible not to fall in love with this city. I will certainly return but hopefully to a much quieter room. One last note: our group was taken to the phosfourescent lagoon in Fajardo. Kayaking through a channel in a mangrove and coming into the lagoon's shimmering waters under a starry sky is an experience I'll never forget.

<Content>Thanks Priceline! My husband and I had a sudden change of travel plans and needed to book a next day lay-over stay in San Juan. Fortunately we were able to get online and book on Priceline! We got this hotel for a bid of $120 a night, a significant savings from the $280-400 per night listed on the Marriott website. We even got a fairly decent room, in the tower on the 7th floor with a partial ocean view (the other part was of some very noisy construction of another high rise hotel right next door, but they lay off work at 5)Let me warn you, tho, the hotel does hit you with a few extra charges beyond what you've already paid thru Priceline, such as a resort fee based on percentage of room price, an occupancy tax of $10, and a parking fee of $14 per day.This hotel is located in the Condado section of San Juan, which is pretty much identical to Miami Beach, including a Starbucks, a Subway Sandwiches, and a Wendy's in the immediate neighborhood, just in case you've been missing junk food.As others have stated, the beach and the hotel grounds are lovely, with the whistling of the coqui frogs at night, and the staff gorgeous and helpful. We didn't explore the bar, casino, restaurant or buffett. We did eat at a 24 hour Puerto Rican diner just down the street, where we tried some very nice goat at a very reasonable price.All in all it was a fun nights stay at a great price for this area!

<Author>NoJokeDee
<Content>It Was O.K. I spent my birthday at the San Juan Marriott Resort  Stellaris Casino in Condado, PR. We stayed for 4 nights in a poolside/oceanview, nonsmoking room on the 10th floor. Overall, it was a beautiful hotel, but there were some problems. First of all, check-in was a nightmare. I was not told before I arrived that there was an additional deposit if you use a debit card instead of a credit card. I went to prepay for my room, but the front desk clerk stated I would have to pay an additional $250 dollars that I did not have. I asked for the manager, and he acted as is he didn't know anything. Eventually, my friend and I paid cash for the room for the first night just to get settled in. The next day was also a bit frustrating because of the deposit requirement. The day manager was willing to work with us; however, she called my room at about 7:00 o'clock in the morning to ask about my credit card, which I thought was VERY rude. Second, there was a small drip coming from the ceiling in the bathroom. The first engineer came and wiped off the ceiling, and told the manager it was condensation. The second engineer said the same thing. Eventually, there were about four different maintenance engineers sent to my room before it was resolved.Third, the water in the bathroom never actually got hot. It was just warm, and I really don't like to take warm showers and baths. They also ran out of washcloths by my second night.NEVERTHELESS, I voiced my concerns to the manager upon checkout and requested to be compensated for the inconveniences. He refunded the cash price I paid for the first night including the resort tax and fees.Overall, I can say this was a pretty nice hotel. I was not excited by the location because it was in a neighborhood that is currently being renovated. There are several other large hotels being torn down, built up or rebuilt, and the construction took away from my view. But the rooms in the Marriott were clean. The rest of the staff was friendly, and the beds were very soft. The pool area was beautiful. It included a waterslide, and the beach was nice; however, the gates to the beach close at about 6:00 pm, and you have to go out to the street if you want access to the beach in the evening. On the weekends, there are live bands that play in the lobby, and they serve food and drinks; but there is also a two-drink minimum and the food is just O.K. The casino was O.K., but I did not see one person really win anything.All guests have 24-hour access to the business center, which includes a daily 1-hour free pass to use the internet and printer. Guests also receive a complementary bottle of water daily, and free access to the fitness center. I was able to borrow an umbrella the day it rained, and the guys working at the Concierge and Rental Car booths were very nice.My suggestions when it comes to staying here: Take the bus when possible. Request a higher floor because of the house band, but not too high because of the construction. Have an open mind, be flexible and don鈥檛 let the small stuff ruin your vacation. Bring a lot of money because things got a bit pricey at times, and study some basic words in Spanish because there are still a lot of people who don鈥檛 speak English. Also, buy water, toiletries and additional film at the Walgreens down the street, and make sure you spend at least one day sightseeing in Old San Juan.If I ever go back to San Juan, I will most likely stay at another property in Isla Verde instead of Condado because of the nightlife. We spent at least $30 dollars a day on taxis going back and forth between Isla Verde or Caroline and Condado. Although there were some decent nightclubs and restaurants near the Marriott in Condado, most of the popular ones were located in the other areas. The San Juan Marriott Resort  Stellaris Casino in Condado is a good hotel for families who just want to relax and who don鈥檛 plan to venture out to the other areas too often.

<Author>fredandkell
<Content>Overall, a pleasant stay! We arrived around 3:00 on a Monday and headed to checkin. We were paying for 2 nights of the vacation ourselves and redeeming 2 nights through Marriott rewards points. Our redemption points were only for a cityview room, but the clerk allowed us to stay in the same room all four nights (the 2 nights we paid for were in a club-level ocean front corner room). We were thrilled by that - we had not wanted to change rooms, and that was a significant upgrade. Our room wasn't ready until 4:00 but they gave us a pager and we hung out in the lobby.The rooms do need upgrading, but hey, that's what they're doing for the next few months, so we knew what to expect. The corner room was large and had two magnificant balconies. The bed was very comfy.The beach was awesome. I don't know why someone said the beach was small - they're crazy!! It is HUGE! Very deep beach, with Hawaii-like sand (very soft and thick granular) and Gulf of Mexico water (even though you're on the Atlantic side, the water is green/blue and very clear). The waves were nice - big enough to give you a thrill, but no nasty undertow. I did hear the water gets pretty rough on this side of the island in the winter. The lounge chairs and umbrellas were a nice touch. The pool was nice; one pool is only 2 feet deep for the kiddies, but I found the beach to be the main attraction anyway.We ate at La Vista - not horribly expensive, typical $12 resort burgers. A decent meal. I recommend walking out of the hotel and going left to eat. (There wasn't much to the right except a Wendy's.) As mentioned in other reviews, Yerba Buena was FANTASTIC! A must-eat! The casino - ho hum. Just not really that exciting. There was only one craps table and it was the deadest, most devoid of life thing we've ever seen. The dealers didn't seem to really know the rules either. We had fun playing roulette, but most people there play slots or blackjack. Low-limit tables were nice ($2 roulette). The casino is expanding another 2,000 square feet to add penny and nickel slots. People complaining about the casino being smoky - have you ever been in a casino that WASN'T smoky?!?! We had been excited to stay in a hotel with a casino, being gamblers, but we didn't spend much time in this one. Also they do not give free drinks to the players!On that note, the club level lounge doesn't have free booze either. I was surprised by this - I thought this was the point of club level!? They have this honor bar system where you can get booze between 5:30 and 7:30 and you write down your name and what you bought and it gets charged to your bill. Drinks were pricey ($6.75 for a local beer). And wouldn't you know it, someone wrote down our name and charged alcohol to our room that we didn't drink and we had to get them to take it off the bill. (You are supposed to sign in every time you use club level. I think someone got our name off the signin sheet and wrote it on the alcohol sheet. Moral of that story - don't bother signing in). The desserts and breakfast in club level were very nice, though.This is a hotel where you definitely want to stay so that you can see the ocean. The other side ain't nothing to look at. I would not stay in the cabana rooms - the tower is the only way to go (after it's done in 2007!). The cabana rooms looked to be much lower quality than the tower rooms and have limited views of the water, even if you are on the ocean side.Overall we were very pleased by the hotel and would stay here again, especially after the renovation. It was a very relaxing experience.

There were big waves and lots of locals with full surf boards and boogie boards, so beware you might get hit when they come crashing down. The waves weren't huge, but you couldn't relax out there, you needed to be alert so you could dive under the waves, or get knocked down. They did have a lot of chairs on the beach and attentive waiters though. They charge way too much money for what they deliver + resort fee. Positives: close to the airport and old san juan. However, I don't think Old San Juan is as quaint as everyone claims. It has like 2 cobblestone streets and everyone acts like it's Europe. It is about 30% gentrified. There are some nice, trendy NY-style restaurants littered between shops that sell random trinkets not from Puerto Rico, We saw lots of shops selling stuff from India, China, and Africa. I recommend Marmalade and Dragon Fly, good food, fun, and fancy drinks. I also recommend going to another hotel!

The hotel did have a reception night, Wednesday, where you got to meet some of the staff and ask any questions about the renovations. They served free drinks and hot appetizers. <Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Loved the Marriott We just returned yesterday from the Marriott. I went with my husband and two young children ages 2 and 4. We had a blast. Our rate was $335 per night from the Marriott website (this included breakfast at La Vista restraunt - a great buffet) First off the service was top notch. I have stayed at top notch hotels much more expensive than this and the service here was much better. They lost one of our bags at the airport and it was waiting in our room when we arrived back from dinner that night. Due to the wine we walked right past it and fell asleep only to notice it the next morning with a message of its arrival (also unnoticed the previous night) on the phone. My son fell and scraped his knee so I called for a band aid. They sent a guy to our room with a big old medical bag to assess the situation and treat the injury with an antibiotic spray and band aid. Our requests for extra towels were met promptly. Out by the pool the staff would remind us of the kids activities that were about to start in case we lost track of time. On the beach we were looking around at the sea of chairs late one morning and a staff came up and asked if we needed help setting up our chairs (they are heavy and it was hot and kids, etc.) So he basically did the whole set up for us including digging a big hole with a shovel for the huge umbrella we also needed. He did not hesitate to run back and get us two more beach towels and run our drink order in to the beach bar. Someone else promtly brought the drinks over to us. All the waitstaff seemed to be experienced in anticipating needs. At the brreakfast even though it was a buffet, our waiter would offer to get a waffle or omlet or whatever for us if there was a bit of a line. Coffee and juice were served almost mmediately when you sat down. Great buffet by the way. They had all the healthy stuff (huge cut up fruit bar, hot cereal, homemade yogurt bagels w/ lox and the trimmings, cold cereal) and all the less healthy stuff (omlet bar, waffels, pancakes, french toast, bacon, potatos, etc.) with a huge bread/muffin spread to boot. The concierge made great recommendations for restraunts (try the Parrot Club and Ropa Vieja for dinner) and made the reservations. Tuscany restraunt was ok but not fabulous. My dish was salty. The Lobby and all common areas were well appointed with marble and brass and spotlessly maintained. The rooms however were your standard Marriott rooms and showed a little wear around the edges. The bathroom was clean but you could tell it was definately not new, which can be a bit unsettling for some discriminating travellers like myself. However the bed was great and bed linens looked new. Overall, the staff seemed happy that we were there and eager to help, but not in a just-trying-to-get-a-tip way. Also, even though the forcast was for partly cloudy with a chance of rain the weather was a perfect 85 and sunny all 5 days we were there! My kids loved the pool and the slide and spent the whole day there. The pool was well maintained but a little on the cold side for me. I also liked the live music poolside on the weekend. WE never went inside the casino so cant comment on that.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Good hotel, but had a couple issues... Just got back from the Marriott in San Juan and really enjoyed my stay there. We booked the room through Priceline and got a really good deal so I was kind of frightened that something might be wrong with the hotel or room, but I was pleasantly surprised.The staff at the hotel were friendly and helpful for the most part. The doormen would always greet me upon returning to the hotel and ask me how I was doing, if I needed anything, etc.We got a room on the 8th floor with an ocean view and balcony. Gorgeous! The maids promptly cleaned our room at 8am every morning (which worked out well since we were usually out on the beach or an excursion by then!) No weird smells or mysterious stains. We always had plenty of fresh towels, wash cloths, etc.The pool was very pretty and never crowded. Perfect for cooling off in after laying out in the sun. The beach was very nice too, but the waves were a little rough there so anyone with young children or who isn't a strong swimmer should be careful.A few complaints about the hotel must be listed. The restaurants in the hotel are INSANELY expensive! Be warned! Almost all of Puerto Rico is overpriced, but the Marriott took that to new levels. At one restaurant in the hotel, La Vista, it was $20 for breakfast - each! $13 for pancakes, $4 for orange juice, and $3 for a cup of coffee. There are lots of other good places to eat in Condado. For breakfast I would recommend Danny's International which is right down the street from the hotel. I got the same breakfast for $6. Look around and bargain shop when it comes to restaurants. The hotel is convenient, but remember you are going to pay dearly for that convenience!In addition to overpriced restaurants, the hotel charged a Resort Fee which they didn't warn us about up front. It ended up being about $10 a day which added up by the end of a week long stay. Supposedly this fee is not optional and covers beach towels and chairs, access to the casino, and a myriad of other complimentary conveniences. Despite being very upset and complaining, the hotel would not budge and reduce my resort fee although I never used a beach towel or a number of the other services it supposedly covered. The Marriott is not a cheap hotel to begin with and I thought this was a somewhat underhanded tactic to get extra money out of its guests. Be warned and make sure to budget for this expense.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great Hotel I had a great time at the San Juan Marriot. Don't be fooled by some of the other reviews, the overall condition of the hotel is excellent. The exterior might be considered 'weathered' but compared to other hotels in the area it is in the best condition. The interior of the hotel is very nice and elegant. Ignore the comments by others, the staff is very helpful. The bell hops are willing to help with directions and food recommendations. They will also arrange taxi service when requested. We asked for a rollaway at check-in and were told we would get it right away. We got a phone call to the room about an hour later asking if it arrived, which it hadn't. We then left for the beach and on our return it was in the room. The housekeepers are also very accomodating. We had the privacy sign on our door for most of the day. Around 2-3PM we received a call asking if we wanted service for that day. We requested more towels which were at our door within 5 minutes of the call. Walking through the hotel, employees would greet us 99% of the time. The condition of the room was excellent, very clean with minimal to no odor (compared to other hotels I've stayed at). As far as noise is concerned, the only sounds we ever heard from other rooms was when the housekeepers were vaccuuming and hit the wall. For me, the only 'negative' was the fridge wasn't that cold and there was no external sink. Neither were deal breakers although a second sink outside of the bathroom does come in the clutch when available. The Casino area is a little small compared to AC and Vegas but it suites the property quite well. There is plenty of room to walk around and not bump into people. There's a fair amount of table games available. The most crowded is the $5 Blackjack tables. Other than that, you won't have much of a problem sitting down a game. Waitresses are readily available at night and are more than willing get you whatever you want.Overall we enjoyed our stay and would return without hesitation.

The lobby is very, very noisy because they have a band playing at night. It is very hard to carry on a conversation because of the band. I pity the staff behind the front desk with that loud noise. It must be bad for your hearing. The hotel is located in a nice section of town called Condado. If you are going to Puerto Rico to play golf do not work with the staff because they know nothing about the sport. --the courses.  My husband and I will not go back to Puerto Rico because the people were not that friendly. There are too many other places to visit again where people bend over backwards to make your stay enjoyable. For instances, Marbella, Spain, Punta Cana, D.Republic, Cancun and Puerto Vallarta.

<Author>WendyW
<Content>Loved Puerto Rico and Marriott Resort I am taking the time to write this review because Tripadvisor has helped me out so much as far as finding good hotels. I think people are easily compelled to write a bad review, but seldom take the time to write a good review. We were pleasantly surprised with Puerto Rico and the Marriott Resort and Stellais Casino. The rooms are 5-star but they are a good solid 4 star. Our first room was on the second floor which I found a little noisy and musty smelling, but they happily changed us to a 9th floor room which was clean, comfortable, and well-suited. We had a beautiful ocean and pool view. The service was wonderful. Everyone was extremely friendly and helpful from the restaurant, front desk, housekeeping, and bellmen. Old San Juan is about 4 miles away. A bus cost 75 cents and a taxi costs $14. Problem is, the bus drives by the hotel about every hour or so. It can be a long wait. Be sure to have exact change or they won't they you on. We had cloudy and rainy weather the 4 days we were there, but we still had a great time. Old San Juan was very quaint. We loved it more than New Orleans (before the hurricane of course). The architecture, bar, shops, people, etc. were great. We had complete strangers ask us if we needed help finding our way around. We felt safe and not threatened at all--even walking around at night in Old San Juan. As you're walking our of the Marriott, make a left down the street. There are plenty of restaurants and shops with better prices and food than the Marriott. We went on the bio-luminescent tour that was coordinated by the Marriott tour guide. It was a lot of fun. Be sure to bring water shoes and wear a bathing suit--you will get wet in your kajak. It's about a 30 minute non-stop paddle out and back so be worned if you're not in shape. We left about 7:00 p.m. and got back to the hotel (via bus) at around 12:45.There is something going on in the bar and nightclub at the hotel every night. We loved dancing to the live band. Even some folks who were staying at the Ritz Carlton (they were on our bio-luminescent bus) couldn't believe how happening our hotel was. The casino is small compared to a Las Vegas casino. We had fun playing 3-card poker. They had slots, blackjack, routlette, craps, etc. There were people of all ages at the Marriott. Mostly Americans and more kids than I thought for late January (Friday through Monday). I love the fact that it only took us a little over 3 hours non-stop (American Airlines) to travel from BWI airport. The hotel was only about 15 minutes from the airport too.The beach wasn't the greatest outside our hotel. It wasn't very big and it's a public beach so it's a little cluttered. They make a lot of effort to keep it clean, but it's still a bit littered. Also, the water wasn't calm when we were there because storms were coming in, but I'm not sure if it would have been much better otherwise. We had 15-20 mph winds while we were there and rainy conditions so it's difficult to tell.We rented a car on Sunday and traveled the island. That's what is nice about Puerto Rico, you're not trapped at your resort. You can travel freely without any problems. My husband is a police officer, so believe me when I say he felt comfortable traveling by car. Ponce wasn't worth stopping by, but we did go to Guanica (Dry Forest)which was pretty nice. We had lunch at the Copamarina Resort which was very quiet and secluded, but there is nothing going on around the resort. The weather was great on that part of the island (southwest) and the water was calm, but there was no place to go other than the resort. At least at the Marriott you could shop, visit Old San Juan, walk around, etc. We will definitely go back to Puerto Rico. Brush up on your Spanish (although everyone spoke at least a little bit of English). Enjoy the friendly people and wonderful atmosphere. We would definitely stay at the Marriott Resort again.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Nice get-away Before I left for my stay, I was always looking at this hotel's review. I have to say that most of them were accurate. I especially found the advise on the trip to the Bacardi Factory. Follow the previous advise. Do not pay for the hotel package trip to the factory, you can do it on your own, by taking the B21 bus to down town San Juan ( stop right outside the Marriot), get off at the last stop down and walk down the hill- turn right to Pier #2 and take the Ferry over for .50 cents. Oh! the bus is .75 cents. make sure and have exact change (No bills). When you get off the ferry, take a right towards a blue building, there will be taxi drivers there that will take you to the Bacardi factory for 3.00....much less than the hotel tour. Coming back, you have to pick up the B21 bus at the terminal to Condado.The hotel stay was great. Very busy and crowded on the weekends, with the locals, who love to dance, so this was entertaining. The staff was pleasant and the concierge was always helpful. Everything is as stated in previous posts. Starbucks across the street with free Wi-Fi. Walgreen鈥檚 right down the street for Misc. stuff like juices and water...Too expensive at the hotel. Be warned that if you will not be using the pool towels, and free water, you do not have to accept the 10% resort fee. The hotel tries to cater for business folks, so the fee is not mandatory, if you are not using all of their services. What else...the food was expensive so if you are on a budget, their are some reasonable American places, Burger King, Uno's etc. We slept most of the time, and got up late, so these were savers for us for dinner. Then we had a nice dinner at Ajili M贸jili, but it was way overprice and the food was noting to write home about. Old San Juan was very nice to visit and walk around and window shop,,,, the prices were not very attractive, since they cater for people visiting on the cruise ships. However, there were plenty of restaurants down town. The cab is $12.00 per trip. We visited the La Plaza American mall...very huge...$12.00 one way in a cab..you can take the same B21 bus, but it take an hour on the bus, as oppose to $12.00 in the cab ( depends on your fancy and time constraints).All in all good get-away for a four day weekend for our anniversary.

The hike is well worth it coz it the most refreshing dip you will have. We took a snorkeling tour, the bus comes and picks you up right from the hotel and it was great way spend the day. We went to Old San Juan a couple of times and always took the bus for 75 cents. We did the Bacardi and the Fort tours ourselves and in my opinion taking the tour would not be worth it. For the Bacardi tour, take the bus to Old San Juan and walk over to the Ferry terminal, take the ferry for 50 cents and take a $3 cab ride from the other side to the distillery. I recommend reading the walking tour if you plan to visit the forts yourself.Overall, people were very friendly and always pointed us in the right direction.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Accomodating staff, beautiful beach, great room! After reading some of the mixed reviews here, I was quite apprehensive before our stay. However, the Marriott very pleasantly surprised me. We paid $175/night for a city-view room (obtained this rate through the Marriott website) but were happy to see that we were placed in a corner room on the 12th floor (1223) which actually had one balcony looking out over the city, but also a side balcony by which we could see the ocean. The bed was extremely comfortable, the shower drain worked properly as did the air conditioner. The beach was beautiful, and we spent most of our time there. We ate in the Italian restaurant at the hotel (Tuscany) -- delicious! Yes, its a little pricey -- but so is most of Puerto Rico. I lived in Rome for a month this past summer so I consider myself a good judge of italian cuisine -- this was excellent. We also dined at La Vista in the hotel for their Carribbean buffett night -- good but not great. We ordered room service one night after getting back from the biluminescent tour -- quite good (and for whoever complained below about 'extra charges' for room service -- I've never stayed in a hotel where they DIDNT charge extra. Its only $2.50, come on)! We ate down the road at Don Jose's Hacienda -- decent, but again not great. Apparently you really need to shell out the $$ in order to get excellent food in this town. We spent a half day in Old San Juan and lunched at Aquaviva -- DELICIOUS. The seared scallops with couscous which is presented in a huge portion like paella and is wonderful. Also go to Bombanera for breakfast -- Puerto Rican bakery packed full of locals, but you can take baked goods and delicious coffee to go. We got 4 pastries and 2 coffees for $6.The staff was extremely accomodating overall. They'd say hi in the elevator, ask how our visit was going, etc. Our maid never entered without knocking. Front desk was excellent, as was the concierge. Pool bar staff will walk out to the beach and take your snack/drink orders so that you never need to leave your beach chair. The casino was as expected. Not huge, not tiny -- this isn't Vegas, so I wasn't expecting the Bellagio. We played Blackjack and Craps and had lots of fun. Definitely take advantage of the free drinks while gaming as we paid $7.50 apiece for Coronas out in the hotel lobby. The lobby is a great people-watching zone once the music starts up -- the locals come in ready to dance and it's quite entertaining to watch.A note on the biluminescent tour -- I was disappointed. I'd recommend going only on a moon-less or almost moon-less night, as the moonlight kinda hindered our view of the glowing plankton. On safety -- I never felt unsafe. The fact that there were so many police cars driving up and down the Condado strip made me feel quite safe. There were single locals jogging at night along the same paths we walked on, which indicated to me that crime wasn't a worry in the area of the hotel.

The rain forests are cool, but you won't see exotic animals or flowers really. Yogi, the hotel guide though is awesome. Do NOT pay the hotel for the Bacardi tour. $35/pp. Instead pay 75 cents for the bus (went up 50 cents)to Downtown San Juan (last stop from the hotel). Walk to Pier #2 ( like a 2 min walk from the bus stop). Take the ferry for 50 cents. Once you're off the ferry, walk to the right and you will see a white building. There are van drivers there who will take you to the factory for $3/pp. With all the money you save, you can buy some Bacardi Rum. The tour is lame, but they have this $50 bottle of Bacardi you can only buy at the factory and no where else in the world. As far as food goes, avoid the Latin Star with your life (it's a few blocks past Walgreen's). Definitely eat at Buena ? I don't speak Spanish, but however you say Green Grass. That place is two blocks up when you walk out of the hotel to the left. AMAZING food! The hotel was nice. Very fancy lobby. Live salsa music at night. We checked in quickly and only had to wait 15 minutes upon check out. Our rooms was cleaned by 9am. Must have been because we were on the 17th floor. The staff was super friendly. Always opened car doors and the hotel door and offered suggestions. They even upgraded our room for free. We had an amazing room (#1717). It was a little small, but man the view was killer. We had TWO balconies--one facing downtown, with a huge construction crane working on a new hotel, blech!, and a view of the ocean. The view of the ocean was breathtaking. Our room also included an awesome FREE breakfast buffet at the Vista (reg price $17/pp.) If you book through the Marriot site directly, it seems most rooms come with this standard. Read the fine print to be sure. Ours just said free breakfast which we assumed was going to be some crappy bagels. Needless to say, we were pleasantly surprised. We ate belgium waffles, made to order omelets, pancakes, sausages, muffins, smoked salmon, mangoes, pineapple, etc. And we just tipped $5 every day. It was great. The casino was a little small, but still fun. Every day before dinner, we went in to play roulette for 10 minutes for dinner money and every night we won $75-175. It was awesome. So every dinner was free. I will say the wait staff at the casino s---, I had to wait forever for my Bacardi and Diet Coke every single time. My last thought, do not leave without eating the fried food downtown from the street vendors. It rocks and for $1.25 it can't be beat. The natives downtown are really friendly too and you can have plenty of friendly conversations.

<Author>OH43944
<Content>Beautiful Views We traveled from Dec.16-22, 2005. We were with a large group, and everyone enjoyed their stay. The temperature was 85 degrees and only one rainy day. Our room was clean, with the most comfy hotel bed we've ever slept in. We had a beautiful 11th floor view of the beach and hotel swimming pool. Unfortunately the balcony was closed off due to construction for most of our stay, but we enjoyed it open the last 2 days. The bathroom was nice,clean and plenty of water pressure and hot water. The maids cleaned our rooms at varying times during the day. Yes, they do open the room without knocking. YIKES! We spent time at Old San Juan, which I highly recommend. The bus is .75 cents, but you might wait 45 minutes to catch a ride. I believe it is the B21 to and from the hotel. It only takes about 12-15 minutes. One evening our group was serinaded by some locals with saxaphone and other local instruments...one lady even danced off the bus. It was a highlight. We took the ferry (.50 c) to the Bacardi Distillery tour. Then $3.00 per person cab fare to the actual distillery. The tour is OK, but most of the group enjoyed shopping at the gift shop and tasting the rum.We had dinner at the Sheraton Cafe one evening with live music and it was fun.Some of our group spent a day at the rain forest,Luquillo Beach and Fujardo. I highly recommend this. We hiked back to the falls and went swimming. The views are breathtaking. We spent several hours at Luiquillo Beach, which has calm waters and beautiful sand. The HIGHLIGHT of our trip was that evening. We went to Fujardo for the BioLuminescent Bay Tour. It was a beautiful evening and we had something to eat right there in a small local outdoors diner. Looked run down, but the food was cheap and good. We kayaked out onto the bay and then thru the channels that take you to a lagoon where we swam. It was awesome to see the sparkles and how your body would light up from these little creatures. The staff (from our tour) was very helpful and kind. It rates a 10 in my book!The hotel staff was friendly and helpful. When we arrived I couldn't open the refrig door, and the bell hop quickly had a new one brought up to the room. They have a safe in each room too. The breakfast buffet was the BEST I've ever seen. The waffles were delicious and the fruit was plentiful. The only rude person working for the hotel that I encountered was one of the morning chefs. There is a Wal-greens just down the street from the hotel, so you can stock up on snacks and water etc. There are Subways everywhere and a Wendy's and Pizza Hut not too far from the Wal-greens if you crave food from home. Security must be a problem in Puerto Rico, because police are everywhere. Some of the local shops near the hotel are locked and they buzz the door open for you to enter. I only drove one day with a rental car. It was an experience. They are not considerate drivers. They blare their horns and it is almost a free for all at their intersections...scary! I would not recommend driving to Old San Juan...there is no parking. The bus is easy and cheap. All in all I enjoyed my 6 days in Puerto Rico. Hope this review helps someone.

<Author>K_Metz
<Content>Christmas week at the San Juan Marriott My wife and I just got back from a week vacation at the San Juan Marriott. Overall, the Marriott met our expectations, which were of a clean establishment with friendly service. We started out in a city view room on a high floor which had an extremely soft bed and non-functioning A/C. After one night in that room, we realized that it was not going to work for us through the whole trip, and they transferred us to a pool view room at no extra charge. It probably wouldn't have been possible later in the week because the resort got much more crowded, but it was good that they were able to accomodate us. The new room was a standard room, nothing extremely fancy, but sufficient. The A/C in this room worked and we still had a soft mattress which was improved by a bedboard. Startdard amenities in the room, although the reports of clogged showeer drains in other reports was true for us as well.We spent most of our time either on the beack or in the casino. The beach was relatively clean, and the only negative was that it got _extremely_ crowded towards the end of our stay and if you did not get out there before 10am, you would have trouble finding a chaise lounge. It seemed like a lot of people staked their claim early with towels on a chair and then went back to bed, which was a bit annoying. But, after a bit of searching, the staff always were able to find a chair for us. Incidentally, there is a hotel next door under construction, and if you came late, you got lunked down right in front of it, which made relaxing a bit more challenging.The casino is relatively small, with probably 10-20 tables for cards, and a couple of roulette and craps tables each and a bunch of slots. The dealers were generally fun and friendly, which made our hours at the blackjack tables (the $5 tables were usually pretty crowded but you could get in eventually) entertaining. The best thing about the resort was the staff. They were extremely friendly and eager to accomodate us at every turn. The rooms could stand some updating, but we were satisfied overall.Location wise, not too bad, safe area, and lots of restaurants nearby, although they tended to be a bit pricey. Starbucks across the street and Walgreens down the block. A few local markets in the area also. Old San Juan is a bus (or $12 taxi each way) ride away. We were only there for a day, but it was a nice strolling part of town and very rustic and vibrant.We were paying the Marriott Friends  family Rate so it was about half of the standard rate. I thin kthat if we were paying the full rate (which was pricey, about $395/night when we were there), it might have been a different story.

<Author>mjburgos
<Content>Overall Exellent Experience My and a buddy stayed at this hotel from 9/26 - 10/17. Overall, it was an excellent experience. I am a native of the island, but haven't been back in many years, and this was the 1st time that instead of staying with family, I stayed at a hotel, and enjoyed the island with minimal family visits. I am fluent in Spanish; my friend does not speak Spanish at all.We booked an Ocean Front room, and at first were disappointed that, unlike many other tripadvisor.com guest, our resort fee wasn't waived. Our room was pleasant, and we have an excellent chamber maid named Marcia, who not only was very good, but gave us a beautiful flower arrangement a few days before we checked out.The beds were nice. Mine was a little on the soft side, but I got used to it and enjoyed it. High speed internet access fluctuates throughout the day (probably based on usage of others), but it was a minor inconvenience.Our room included breakfast, and by the end of the 1st week we knew all the restaurant staff by name. They were great, and made breakfast a lot of fun for us. We dined at Tuscany once, and it wasn't bad at all, however for $140 I expected a little better, but that might be the New Yorker in me talking. The room service menu was unusually boring, but luckily we only did that once, because of a lack of energy to go out one night.We rented a car for this trip because of meetings we had in Ponce and other points far away. Parking at the hotel was easy, and on weekends we found ourselves on the higher floors but that was no big deal. The cabbies congregate on the B level and have some benches set up; stop and listen in one day as they pontificate on all matters of life and death. Negotiate your cab fare before leaving the hotel, or any other point on the island. All the cabs have meters, and not a single time did we see one turned on.The concierge staff was knowledgeable and friendly, except one, and I wish I could remember her name. She was more focused on finishing her conversation with a coworker than helping me. But I turned to another staffer there and got what I needed, and made a complaint, which seemed to be addressed immediately.Getting to Old San Juan from this hotel is super easy--walk down the block to the right, take the B21 bus for 25 cents, and you are there in a few minutes....that is, after waiting forever for the bus to come. A cab will cost $10-$12, so the wait and price are worth it. If you are a coffee lover, have a great cup of cafe con leche at la Bombonera on Calle San Francisco (have it with a piece of flan while you're at it). I have been going there since a child. I also highly recommend the Parrott Club in Old San Juan for dinner (on La Fortuleza, near several other chic dinner spots).The spa and exercise room staff were really great. Very friendly and very open to sharing places to go and see. Daniery was my masseuse and also did a pedicure for me. She is very nice. Practice some Spanish first before you see her. My feet never looked so good.My room came with a balcony which was closed due to renovation. I got 5,000 Marriott points for each night there because of this, which was worth it. A quick trip on the elevator downstairs gave me all the fresh air I needed.Nightlight at the hotel was fun. For example, Wed - Sun had live bands, and they were all excellent. I didn't stay to dance there, but would have 1 or 2 drinks and the energy and music put me in the right mood to go out and look for trouble and the local clubs. Weekends really fill up there at night, especially in the casino. Doormen were polite and quick to get us taxis (for nights we planned on drinking).If you are traveling with kids, there are plenty of kid-friendly restaurants. Sizzler is a long walk or short cab ride away. Chilli's isnt a long walk at all. Pizza Hut seemed a little greasy, but was only a block from the hotel, as was Wendy's. Venture a little further down Ave Ashford and you will find Fudruckers and Pizza Uno....I avoided most of these, as I can eat all that garbage here in NYC. I wanted good, local food. Walk over to Ajili Mojili for a great dinner, very puerto rican. My advice--just walk up and down Ave Ashford your first day there, get to know the area, and grab a paper copy of all the locally owned restaurant menus.In summary, I highly recommend this hotel. The staff were very friendly, very helpful, and quick to our service. My buddy had no trouble speaking only English to the staff. We both have to return on business in January to the Condado area--we are definitely staying here again!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>One of the top San Juan Hotels I am one of those that drives myself crazy reading all the reviews of a place and then go nuts trying to find a place without a bad review. I've learned to really take those bad reviews with a grain of salt.The hotel isn't as glamorous as say the Wyndham, but that doesn't mean it's sub-par. The beach is fantastic (many hotels in San Juan have sub-par beaches) - the two level pool has a swim up bar, a fun slide, plenty of chairs and wireless internet all over (included in your resort fee - which I do consider just bad business, but everyone is doing it.)The casino is adequate, the slots aren't up to most mainland standards and the placement of everything is a bit tight, but the service is friendly and the tables draw a mixture of tourists and locals.There is always a party in the lobby. Bands that go all night, huge crowds on the weekends and over priced drinks to make you feel right at home.I haven't even gotten to the two best things about the hotel - the staff and the location. The staff was extremely friendly and helpful and no reasonable request wasn't given their full attention, you were made to feel at home.The best part though was the location. The streets of Condado are lined with fabulous restaurants and shops. Pizza Huts, Burger King, Subway, Citibank, Starbucks and Walgreens are all with in a block or two. The local restaurants are top notch and plentiful. Access to Old San Juan is either a 10 min bus (if your lucky enough to catch one) or cab ride. The police seem to be everywhere and I didn't feel unsafe at any point and we walked all over, every night.Overall, if you stay here, you will walk away happy.

If you like beer try Medalla Light, it is a Puerto rican beer, I am not a big beer drinker but I feel in love, it's so good that I'm in NY trying to find out why no one imports to the USA. Make sure you visit Old San Juan and the mall both easy to get to. In summary the hotel is cool, Condado is cool but in my opinion PR is not some where that you go for more than 4 days and it's not a first class island so keep that in mind and you'll have fun.

<Author>daisie152
<Content>Had a good time in Puerto Rico HOTEL:We arrived at the San Juan Marriott and entered the lobby by 11:30 a.m. on September 1, 2005. I did not find the lobby to be grand or impressive at all. You enter the hotel looking at a bar with a bunch of tables surrounding it. To the right is the casino and to the left is the check in counter. I don't know why but I found this quite ODD!We were immediately able to check into our upgraded room. We were upgraded to a suite that was located on the second floor overlooking the pool, ocean and a little side road. Our room was nice and big!!!The pool was ok. The water was alittle cloudy. They had two pools. One for little kids and one for bigger kids. We mostly sat in the kiddie (no more then three feet deep) pool just to cool off. The slide was fun though!! The patio was quite nice too.The beach was really nice!! The ocean is alittle rough but we had a great time riding the waves.The area surrounding the hotel was very peculiar and seedy!!!!! There was a huge security presense. Some of the buildings were in dire need of a face lift. A lot of buildings were boarded up and some of them were just in really bad shape.FOOD:We ate at the marriott once. We had breakfast at their outdoor restaurant. It was good. We ate at the surrounding restaurants that were located off site. The prices were moderate and the food was good. ACTIVITIES:We took the East Wind Catamaran to Culebra Island. DO this trip. It was fantastic and Flamenco Beach is Beautiful!!!Old San Juan - Had a great time walking around the city. The city has a lot of character and is very picturesque.El Yunque - If you have seen a rain forest before I would skip this one. It was nice but its not worth the time or money to see it.Bioluminescent tour - Now this one....the idea is awesome. It is cool to see and experience this. Getting to and from the bay is a nightmare!!!!!!!!!!! It's pitch black dark. We had motor boats and other kayakers running head on into us. I think there needs to be a mandate for the number of people who are allowed into the bay at once.LITTLE TID BITS:Please be aware that Marriott charges an extra $17 per night resort fee on top of the room rate. This adds up after a few nights. I wish we knew this.The wait staff at all the restuarants try to up sell the menu and try to get you to order extra stuff. Know what you want and try not to be persuaded.If you do go to El Yunque...think about renting a car and going to El Yunque early afternoon and then do the Bioluminescent tour that same night. This saved us the cost of a dinner. approx. $70.There is no set cab fare to go anywhere.....what ever they feel like charging as the wind changes is what they charge. Long story short just be aware that the cab fares are not consistent and do add up.If you have access to the lobby on the Executive level DO take advantage of this. The spread they put out each day (excluding weekends) was impressive. Um...I think thats it. I hope this helps you and gives you some extra information you may not have known.Overall, I did think the Marriott was a fine hotel and when I return I will consider staying there again. I'm thinking I may want to go live on Culebra Island though.Best regards and happy vacationing to all.
