<Author>hbyerly
<Content>Feeling hot, hot, hot We stayed in room 1411 on a marriott rewards stay the last week in August. The hotel wasn't very full, and they upgraded us without charge to an ocean view on check-in.The room was typical Marriott - clean, decent furnishings, mattresses with foam toppers, the ubiquitous green/beige carpeting. The a/c disconnects when the balcony door (gorgeous view) is opened, so you have to be careful to close it tightly to keep the room cool. A/C was barely adequate, despite having the engineer check it twice. It cooled to about 73F, but because it is centralized it did nothing for the humidity. We kept it going the entire stay and clothes still came out of drawers damp.The hotel has lots of amenities - the pool is lovely, with a good mix of sun and shade. There is a nice workout room (no charge for guests) with a variety of equipment, and the spa offers a small menu of massages. The hotel advertises wireless internet, but it was not available in our room (though I saw people using it in the lobby). There is an extra charge for Internet access, about $10/day, slightly less by the week. There's also a self-serve laundry facility, which is important because everything is so damp.There's a very small casino off the lobby, and the lobby bar had live music most evenings.The beach is fantastic - a wide swath of sand with clean water, but though the surf was fun for body surfing it was too rough for snorkeling or just floating around. They keep the red flag (dangerous water conditions) up year-round as there is no lifeguard on the beach. They do have waiters on the beach who circulate fairly often.The on-site restaurants were good - the Vista has a buffet going pretty much all the time, and you can also order from the menu. Lunch/dinner is about $45 for two people, which we thought was reasonable given the variety and location. The Tuscany is more high-end (i.e. the waiters are better dressed), and the food was mixed, with some things quite good and others less so.There are couple of restaurants within walking distance - the hotel is on a strip of major hotels that are mixed in with smaller guesthouses and restaurants. I've read other reviews comparing the area to South Beach, but I think that's a very poor comparison. There's a Walgreens a half block away (turn right out the front door), which is good for water and snacks.The location is Condado, just a few minutes east of old San Juan. It's about a 10 minute taxi ride, and they charge $12-14 depending on what part of the city you're heading toward.The staff is extremely nice, with the exception of the gift shop and tour staff, who seem to think that guests were an inconvenience.Bottom line - this was our first visit to PR, and we enjoyed the Marriott very much. I probably wouldn't come again at this time of year - it rarely got below 90, and with the high humidity it was uncomfortable to be outside for too long. For our next visit I'll try a guesthouse in a less urban area, I would not pay the rack rate of close to $300/night (I used points) for this property.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Okay stay, not impressed My husband and I stayed at the Marriott for a long weekend. This was a last minute weekend trip for my husband and me, so we did minimal research. Do yourself a favor and research your destination, especially if you have limited time. This is not a place to stay if you do not have kids. Well, the beeper never beeped so we went back to the desk at 4 o'clock, which is the check-in time, and our room was ready. The man who gave us our room key not friendly at all. Brian at the lobby bar was very nice, as was Gerry, who kept the lobby area very neat and clean. The bartenders that were at the lobby bar on Friday night were terrible. It was difficult to get a drink and difficult to get the check. We had breakfast at one of the restaurants on Saturday and we were completely rushed through the meal. Don't get the breakfast buffet on the weekend. The line is so long at the omelet station that the rest of your food will be cold by the time your eggs are cooked. The hotel needs serious updating (which is in the process of occurring). Our room was comfortable and clean, however, one day housekeeping did not clean our room until after I spoke with the housekeeping supervisor (at 5:00 p.m.). Don't bother with the hotel gift shop, people who work there are less than welcoming. Don't expect most of the staff in general to be overwhelmingly friendly to make you feel welcome or that you are glad that you booked the hotel. If you plan on staying for a romantic weekend, think about staying elsewhere. Also, plan on going off of the Condado if you really want to have a good time. The best meal we had was at El Convento in Old San Juan. If we do return to San Juan, we will stay at at more upscale hotel like El Convento and take day trips off the Condado. Also, the entire Condado area is in flux. There are massive construction projects underway on Ashford Avenue.

<Rating>2	2	3	-1	3	-1	2	-1	

<Author>JDERV
<Content>A Fair Review of SJM OK, lots of negative messages regarding the San Juan Marriott on this board. Having stayed at this hotel approx. 20 times during the past 5 years, I feel I have some balanced perspective.My most recent stay was in April 05. The hotel facility was previously a different hotel (Diplomat) which was destroyed by a fire in the mid 80's. Marriott bought the building and renovated in the late 90's. Many of the ongoing renovations are replacement activities from the original hotel (such as old windows and doors). Prior to initiating major renovations, particularly to the rooms, both the website and the hotel advise all guests.I agree that during the past few years the service has been spotty. Sometimes good/sometimes bad but honestly more often good. I have never found any part of the facility (hotel, gym, casino) to be run down. In fact there is constant cleaning occuring in the common areas of the hotel.there The rooms are of varying size but I have never stayed in what I'd consider a small room. In the tower section of the hotel it is better to stay on floors 14 and higher because there is some noise from the lobby music - also the cabana wing is less noisy. The beds are very comfortable (soft mattress) and the housekeeping and overall upkeep has always been excellent during my stays.The pool area is quite attractive with nice landscaping, chairs, umbrellas and wait service for drinks. People who are complaining about excessive children most likely were visitng during school holiday time. I have not experienced an overwhelming number of out of control children at the pool. The beach area is public beach (city of San Juan) and not owned by the Marriott - however the hotel does provide chairs and umbrellas. The water is clean, particularly for an urban setting however there is a serious under-tow/rip-tide possibility at this beach - BE CAREFUL when swimming.The restaurants and room service are expensive - in fact I think more expensive than comparable restaurants in SJ. However in the immediate area of the Marriott (within 1/2 mile walking) are many restaurants from mid-range chains (Uno) to fine dining (Ramiros). There are also 2 Japanese restaurants within close distance (1 next to the hotel). I have never felt unsafe walking in the Condado area of San Juan - even late at night.I have found that in the past year, the SJ Marriott rates are almost always on the high-end (rarely less than $225 per night for city view room). In the past there were more frequent weekend specials and I've stayed for as little as $140 per night. For the current rates charged, there are other hotels in the city (Ritz Carlton or Intercontinental) which might provide a better experience for the money.Bottom line - if you're spending more than $225-250 and seek a true luxury experience then spend a little more and stay at the Ritz Carlton. If you want a relaxing stay in a clean, comfortable hotel with many options for dining outside the hotel AND you can get a rate of $225 or less, then I'd recommend the SJ Marriott.

<Author>aos200
<Content>Coonstruction! - Travel Agent's review I am pretty amazed after reading the positive reviews on this website and visiting the Marriott firsthand. Did no one see what we saw? I must say that I will never book anyone in the Marriott, San Juan especially but probably not the Condado area as well. Here's why.First off, be forewarned that construction in the San Juan area (including Old San Juan and Candado) is rampant and EVERYWHERE - as are the problems that come along with it in any city, namely; traffic, noise, congestion. If this statement alone is enough to make you question San Juan as a place you'd like to vacation peacefully - trust your instincts and book a hotel at an alternate location in PR outside of the San Juan city area (Dorado, Isla Verde or farther) or choose an alternate island in the carribbean.As for the Marriott itself, and I am AMAZED no one has really made a point of this, THE HOTEL ITSELF IS UNDERGOING A 4 PHASE RECONSTRUCTION ON THE WEST END AND ON THE PROPERTY IMMIDIATELY EAST A HOTEL IS BEING BUILT THROUGH 2006. This means that unless you want a view of a construction site, your only bet is the middle-back of the hotel that overlooks the pool. Now if your room assigned does not have a working balcony as a result of the work being done, you are entitled to 5000 marriott points per night or a $100 food and beverage credit per night (sign upon checkin). This means that if you stay on the West side of the hotel where they are painting and renovating the outside and therefore your balcony is locked for safety and out of use, you are entitled. Unfortunately, if your balcony is functional (as was ours, although it overlooked a construction pit and 2- 100 foot cranes to the East. I am sadly not kidding), we did not apply for the credit. Of other notes, our room was 2-3* quality, so be forewarned the high stars given on tripadvisor are indeed misleading. While I understand the level of sophistication is generally not as high in the Carribbean as it is elsewhere, the reality is our room was not the usual Marriott quality (ie. clean, comfortable). A 4* hotel does not have mold growing around the caulf of the tub, our bedding looked shabby, the bathroom needed a desperate regrout, and our balcony had cheap plastic furniture that looked about 10 years old. I could deal w that - after all, how long are you really in a room? But After speaking to the manager and explaining we were not informed of the construction when booking the hotel (which is right next to the beach - you MUST be able to hear it when outside during the day), I was still not offered ANY type of compensation or apology because I was 'upgraded' to a room with a balcony. An insult, to say the least, being our balcony overlooked a pit and construction cranes. I responded by informing the manager the hotel booking policy of not informing guests of the construction, and then not compensating those they deem 'unaffected' is not good business and I would not recommend such a property to my clients. To which I was told to my amazement 'that's fine, do not book your clients here'. Which leads me to ask - if this is the way the hotel manager treats an agent, how would he treat a poor client ? This is not to imply that the manager's attitude prevails in terms of the rest of the Marriott employees - that would be unfair. But when I go away on vacation, I expect a few basic things - namely, clean sheets, a clean bathroom, and a quiet place to relax and read a book or nap. Unfortunately after an hour at the Marriott, it seemed clear to me none of these things would happen without an excruciating effort that would defeat the point of my vacations. So I cut my losses and I checked out.As for the pool, we never swam but it looked very nice. The beach we never made it to so I cannot comment. The casino was a typical hotel casino (a bit smaller than I expected). The lounge bar was very active however the music was too loud (and I like music!) to hear the person next to you. Be forewarned there is a 'resort fee' or $10 a day and also a daily parking fee of $18 per day if you decide to stay here. As far as the Condado 'strip', we were told of the many nice restaurants on the outside of the hotel but we walked the strip and found nothing other than local 2* joints. Not that that is ever necessarilly a bad thing - but just as I expect the cons of a city (ie. noise, traffic, etc), I expect the pros as well (more sophisticated areas, better dining, etc). I am a 26 year old girl and I would not have felt safe walking alone had my boyfriend not been there to be honest. (There is a little, shady strip club across the street and 5 doors down from the Marriott).All in all, I must say that I recommend no one stay at this hotel or Condado in general. The city of Old San Juan is not very big and there is no real benefit to staying near it - the traffic is horrendous, there is construction everywhere, I assume there is rampant poverty as we saw a ton of shanty areas and 'for sale' signs, and even strolling down the streets you will be continuously bombarded by people in their cars and on their scooters playing excessively loud music. (I live in Manhattan and don't need to leave the motherland to enjoy that). If you do go, you can see El Morro and el castillo and enjoy lunch or dinner and some shopping around all of Old San Juan in half a day. As far as nightlife, we were only in old San Juan for a night, but didn't see many options other than 5 or so nice restaurants. (So if nightlife is your thing, this is not your place - go to South Beach, Cancun, stay at Atlantis, etc).Most resorts outside of San Juan do not charge their guests parking and by the time you add up taxi fees and tour transportation charges (for example, if you travel to el yunque (the rainforest), it is $50 per person for the bus tour, a cab from the airport to Candado is $15 each way). Therefore, my strong suggestion is to rent a car and just get out of San Juan - stay elsewhere on the Island. We ended up at the Hyatt Dorado which was lovely - I will post a review for that.Hope this helps give you a more detailed view of the Marriott/Condado area.

<Author>LisaNewYork
<Content>Marriott has changed a lot since the last time I went there.. I've stayed at the San Juan Marriott 5 years ago and enjoyed my stay. However, this time around was totally different. The hotel staff itself is very friendly. They open doors and are very courteous. That's never a problem. But the hotel is run down and definitely needs repairs which we knew before we decided to stay there. I believe the repairs are being made the first week of June. The pool area is small. There were tons of kids the week I stayed here and very unruly as well. They did not adhere to the rules of the pool area. They were jumping and diving into the pool which was prohibited; they were climbing up the water slide after the lifeguard was off duty and they were throwing volleyballs at each other. The hotel staff did absolutely nothing to reprimand them. The swim up bar shuts down at 4:00 p.m. - after that, you have to get out of the pool and walk to the outdoor bar if you want a drink. It's very loud and noisy. If you want a quiet place to relax and enjoy the beach and pool, DO NOT stay here. On weekends, the beach can get very crowded. If you're not out very early, your chance of getting beach chairs and an umbrella are very slim. I also witnessed nudity on the beach which I don't think is appropriate for a family hotel. Also, we made 2 reservations with the concierge for dinner, which were NOT made. We had to confirm with them and it's a good thing we did, otherwise we would not have had reservations. If you want good Puerto Rican food - eat at Ajili Mojili - they have great Mofongo. Ropa Vieja is also very good. Another excellent restaurant is Ramiro's. This place is an upscale Spanish restaurant and is walking distance from the hotel. I would make reservations. The rooms for the most part are decent size and are clean. I recommend staying on a higher floor because of the nightlife downstairs in the hotel lobby. They have singing, dancing, bands etc which was nice. The trip to Camuy Caves is nice but is definitely NOT worth the $90 the Marriott charges you compared to other hotels that charge $74. If you're planning to go to El Yunque, my suggestion is to rent a car and go yourself. The tour guide will not do half the things the rain forest offers. My overall opinion of this hotel would be just okay, maybe average. The next time I go back, I may think of staying elsewhere.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great Vacation - But Not Fabulous I booked this trip 4 months in advance after reading reviews. I originally wanted to stay at the InterContinental but couldn't find a great rate and like the location of the Marriott better. We got a rate of $179/night because the reservations center made an error. That in itself was a hassle. But onto the vacation...I was meeting a friend there from Boston and she arrived first, checking into a smoking, ocean-front room. The only reason we stayed was because it DID NOT smell like smoke - we are both non-smokers but loved the view. Unfortunately, the hotel said they did not have any other ocean front rooms available in non-smoking so we would have been stuck in city-view if it had smelled. We had a housekeeping issue the first night as well, finding hair in the bed and in the shower that was not ours, and immediately called the front desk. The hotel did show great customer service in giving us a $100 credit at the Italian restaurant on site. (More on that later) But at check-out, it showed a small charge from the restaurant that we had been told had been covered...was resolved, but an added hassle. Other than the hair, the room was fine, the beds were comfortable and it was clean.Tuscany, the italian restaurant, is AMAZING. Not only is the service fabulous, but the food is wonderful. We had pasta with lobster, ossa bucco, grilled salmon, seared tuna and loved our meals....Definitely go there if you are in town whether you stay at the restaurant or not.The rest of the trip was fine...the pool was crowded as it was a holiday weekend and there were lots of kids but that didn't bother us. The only issue at the pool is finding a sunny place to be for the day. The hotel placed palm trees all over the pool area and they block the sun depending on where you sit. The beach is all open and they have lounge chairs and umbrellas although if you like long walks on the beach, this is not the place for you. I enjoy walking the beach to exercise and there's not too far to walk. There is a great band at night in the lobby and a casino in the hotel(a few $5 and $10 tables for blackjack). Plus you can walk to a bunch of restaurants and bars on Ashford Ave. We went into San Juan twice and it's a $10 cab ride and great to walk around and try some restaurants! Maria's is a local place for frozen drinks, The Parrot Club and sister restaurants are fun and if shopping is your thing, there is a Coach Factory store there!The only other major issue was the concierge. They are not the most helpful and don't make too many good recommendations. I suggest researching the area on your own before you go.If I go back, I'll try to stay at the IC unless the price is much better at the Marriott.

<Author>reed13ja
<Content>Nice on the inside, but looks a little shabby outside My husband and I stayed here for three nights after a cruise. The hotel is large and nice, and the service is very friendly. The only problems we had were with the outside of the building and the neighboring buildings. Be careful when booking here in the summer of 2005. They are doing construction and painting on the balconies and outside walls of the hotel - which it badly needs. But this could add up to a lot of noise! The hotel is also surrounded by construction of other buildings on both sides, and the whole area of the beach is a little shabby.Speaking of the beach, if you are bringing kids, be careful! The water is VERY rough and has a strong undertoe. Few parents would let their children swim, and if they did the kids stayed in the water for no more than five minutes. I still have sand in my ears from the huge waves knocking me down! In fact, local kids came to the beach in front of our hotel to surf. On the other hand, the pool is great for kids and there are activities planned daily. The hotel resteraunts are so-so, a little overpriced in my opinion. The area has a few nice local places as well as chain resteraunts. KFC delivers to the hotel if you really miss home-cooking! The hotel is close to Old San Jaun which is a great trip. Also, there is a tour desk that plans reasonably priced tours to local attractions. They offer trips to the rainforest, the Bacardi distillery, Old San Jaun, and moonlight kayaking. The hotel does have a nice casino, but it is a little small! Don't expect anything like Vegas.I would have given this hotel an above average rating, but the price was a little too high. Next time I will try another beach in Puerto Rico, one that is more conducive to laying out and swimming in the ocean.

I would suggest to do a 1/2 day in old San Juan or more. Dont go on Sunday evening, the shops close by 5 or 6. All in all the trip was great, next time I would definately not stay in San Juan. OBTW...the Intercontinental, ESL, Hilton looked great.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Marriott San Juan, Not great but still pretty good My wife and I just got back yesterday from the Marriott San Juan. It was not great but it was pretty good and we had a wondeful time. I had read reviews on this board before leaving and was not sure what to expect. In the end I was plesantly surprised. First let me say that I have stayed in a variety of hotels from really cheap to some of the best including Four Seasons and Ritz. I mostly stay in Marriotts on business and amassed some points to use for this particular stay. I do not expect Marriotts to be 5 star establishiments. They are not competing with super high end luxury hotels so if that's what your used to.. forget it. The service is not as solicituous and the small details and overall experience of a Four Seasons is not what you're going to get. Having said that,h it was still nice.The hotel is in pretty good condition with the common areas very clean and well kept. The hotel has begun their renovation and crews were in the process of painting the exterior. Our room (city view) was fine. Clean, reasonable size but was a little dated. We were on the 5th floor. Word of warning: if you are in the main tower and go to bed early, you want to be high ie.. 8th floor plus. The night club in the lobby gets VERY loud and we could here the base thumping as late as 3am on saturday night! Pool is very nice, lots of young kids, but better that than crawling with spring breakers. Also, the whole pool area is in full sun by about 11am unless you are under a palm tree.Service was very good at the pool with people regularly circling to see if you wanted a $7.50 frozen drink or a $12 burger. Hey, it was expensive but it's a resort! The only truly bad service we had was a surley attendant at the beach who didn't have his story straight about whether to charge us $12 for an umbrella or not. If you are being charged the resort fee of 10% per night then the umbrellas are free. We were not being charged the fee as we were using points so we had to pay for the umbrella. Oh well, the 12 bucks was less than 10%. As far as I could tell, the 10% resort fee does not seem to cover anything else of importance so better you pay for the umbrella. The beach itself is clean, big, not crowded and the water is beautiful. Their is some surf but not too bad. My wife and I both had massages. She said hers was great. Mine was o.k. At $100 a pop they are pretty pricey. The spa was very clean although the lockers were not fuctional. But the massage rooms and atmosphere were nice. Again, it's not the Four Seasons.The area of Condado is great. It is kind of like south beach Miami but not as upscale. Nice stores and o.k. restaurants. I would recommend Tijuanna for great mexican food and the Mariachi band. Yeuba Buena was not bad. Danny's has very good pizza and breakfast. Everything is pretty expensive, figure, $70 bucks for two people for an average meal with a couple of drinks. We also hit the Burger King down the street for Breakfast. It was cheap and quick. We ate one nite at La Mallorcina. Recommended by the concierge. Not very good, don't go. Pricey, small portions of average food. Also check out Piu Bello Gelato. Great deserts and Ice Cream at a reasonable price.The only outside activity we did was a Catamaran/Snorkel trip aboard the SpreadEagle II. Don't let the name fool you. This was a very professional crew who did a great job. We actually sailed (most of these boats just moter to save time). We went to two beautiful beaches on the same island for great snorkeling and actually fed fish by hand with bread left over from lunch. You get all you can drink Pina Coladas and Rum Punch as well as soda and water. Lunch is a sandwich buffet which didn't sound all that big of a deal but turned out to be very good. Lots of fixings, everything laid out fresh along with fruit and salad. All of this for $77 per person. I can't say enough about the crew. They were fun, professional, courteous, and worked very hard to make sure everyone had a geat time.Overall our vacation was great. Puerto Rico is more like a carribean island than a 51st U.S. state. Many people speak little or no English and the standard of living is low with some areas we drove through looking very 3rd world. Way to much on this board is made of the hotel's surrounding area being scary unclean or full of Graffiti. The Condado area is clean, seems very safe and the graffiti was limited to buildings that are in the process of being demolished to make way for more luxury property. Overall we found it a very convienient area to be in with much within walking distance and only a 10 min cab ride to the airport. Hope this helps!!

<Content>Needs a lot of updates but great location The hotel is in a great location. We had access to the concierge level during the day and they were nice there. It was worth getting breakfast there as breakfast in the hotel is really expensive. You might as well save your money for better restaurants outside of the hotel. The maid service is poor. We came back from being out all day to find our room not made up, it was annoying considering we were tired and wanted to take a shower, instead we had to wait for the maid service to clean our room.The hotel could be a great place and hopefully with the renovations, they will upgrade its look inside and out. If you are looking for location in terms of being near the city and near the beach, this is your place. But search for the cheapest deal (rooms are way too overprices), no one should pay a ton of money to stay here. Stay at the Ritz if you want luxury and want to pay a similar price.

There are two pools, both large, however they were both crowded with kids. The pools are nice and large, but are blocked by the hotel during much of the morning, so until noonish, they are in the shade. In the afternoon, the pools do get more sun. The resort is located in a great spot, there is a Starbucks right across the street and Dunkin Donuts, Pizza Hut, Walgreens only a few blocks away. The staff was nice, service was good. Oh and we had a GREAT dinner at the restaurant Tuscany in the hotel. All in all a good experience, would go back. The hotel is going through renovations starting in May 05 through Sept. 05.

<Content>Nice Place One word - TOURISTYWe prefer off the beaten path kind of vacations - far from the maddening crowds. The rooms are immaculate, clean and well stocked. The views from the hotel are amazing.There was a latin band playing in the lobby and we tried practising our Salsa and Merengue with the locals and the rest.The casino is small but gets crowded.The beach is conveniently located right behind the hotel. They do check your claim for re-entry into the hotel premises (flashed our room card to the bouncers/guards)The pool is beautiful. The shallow pool is too shallow for adult swimming, and the second pool gets crowded with kids during the afternoons. Nevertheless it's a wonderful place to just hang out, get a tan, catch up on reading, and peoplewatch.The restaurants are good too. They had two buffets - one being the 'healthy choice' and the other being everything.Parking is $14 for a 24 hour period.There's a bus (21B, i think), that runs past the bus stop right outside the hotel for 25c and takes you right into Old San Juan. We however pooled in $2 per person and took a 6 person cab in. It's slightly faster since it doesn't make stops.The airport is about 15 minutes away. If you rent a car and opt to return a full tank, make sure you gas up before you hit the highway that takes you into the airport. We expected to see a gas station right before the rental return, but did not find any. We then opted to get out of the terminal to fill up and return only to get late to check in our luggage (which meant I had to give up my expensive Swiss Army knife that would not have made it through security as carry on luggage :(I digress...The staff at the hotel is helpful and professional.All in all a really well managed place with a ton of amenities - in the room and out (on the hotel premises)However, at $275 a pop, I'll wait a few hundred years and accumulate enough points for another stay in paradise.

<Author>HazMat71
<Content>Very Impressed with the San Juan Marriott Resort  Just returned from a five day stay at the San Juan Marriott Resort  Stellaris Casino and was very pleased with all aspects of the resort. The staff was wonderful and the concierge service was invaluable. One suggestion is to pay the extra money or if you are a Rewards member get access to the Executive Level Lounge. Very nice and had food and drink most of the day into the evening. We had a deluxe corner oceanfront room which had a king size bed (extremely comfortable) and we requested a roll away which was delivered promptly. The pool is great for kids and spending your whole trip there would not be disappointing. The pool water was comfortable. You did have to move from time to time to chase the sun but this was not a very big issue since tanning is no problem. As a matter of fact be careful of the sun and sun block is highly recomended. The beach is beautiful and the access was great. The undertoe can be dangerous but don't hold your kids back. Just watch them and restrict some of the distance they enter the water. The water is warm and blue. Contruction is all around but was not very noticable and in no way distracted from the resort atmosphere. The locals were very friendly and helpful. Expect pretty slow service in the local restaurants but venture out and taste the local fare. It is delicious. If you have kids get the pizza at Danny's which was delicious and carry out was convenient and cheaper than the hotel which serves a 7-11 type pizza. Go to Walgreen's and buy your bottled water for your stay and liquor/beer in town. Go on the snorkeling trip, visit the rain forest (our tourguide Ed La Joy was excellent! request him if possible) and visit the forts and shop downtown. Cigar Afficionados must go to Don Collins Cigar Shop downtown for some locally grown tobacco cigars which were great after a heavy local meal. The casino is fun and paid for most of the trip. I felt safe in every aspect of our stay. Security is everywhere and we heard of no issues. Downsides- The rooms are a bit dated and wear and tear is present. It is time for some renovation which I understand is coming. The hotel needs to improve their game room to accomodate more kids. Bottom Line- My family is eagerly awaiting the opportunity to return. We saw several other hotels in the area which were as beautiful some even more so but for a family will return to the Marriott.

Old San Juan: Everyone just strolls the boardwalk and streets at night on the weekends. <Content>San Juan and the Marriott Stellaris great for whole family! We just got back from San Juan's Marriott Stellaris Hotel and Casino. We had a great stay! Head down the street (to the left of hotel) to Danny's for a cheap and wonderful breakfast alternative to the hotel. Go a little farther down the street to a convenient store to replenish your mini-bar cheaply! San Juan is a big city so expect big-city activity (traffic on Saturday night, a beggar here and there, and fast-food chains). I thought the streets where impeccably clean. And yes, there are some hotels under construction in the area. But none of that disturbed our stay in the least. Do your best to seek out the local food. While not for waistwatchers, the local cuisine is delicious. Pamela's at the Numero Uno guest house was a superior upscale dining experience that was also grade-school-age kid friendly. Ajili Mojili was also excellent for getting a superbly prepared Puerto Rican meal. Parrot Club somewhat disappointing (couldn't talk over music).

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Perfect Choice for Condado If you're staying in the Condado -- there is probably no better choice of hotel than the Marriott. I've been visiting PR for 20 years now and one has to pick your location carefully. Old San Juan? Isla Verde? Condado? It all depends what you're looking for. My partner and I prefer Condado these days for several reasons. First, there is plenty to do in the Condado area including the beach, restaurants, nightlife, casinos, etc. It's close to the old city (closer than Isla Verde) and unlike Isla Verde there are places to walk around. (Condado is also walking distance to the better beaches in Ocean Park).The Marriott itself is a fine hotel with all the amenities you would expect from a first class resort hotel. Try to upgrade to a corner room and you will never forget this hotel -- huge windows, sweeping views, breakfast on the balcony -- it's always a great way to start the day. The place is generally very clean, the staff is professional, the food is fine (but there are plenty of places to eat nearby) and overall the hotel is a good value.Unlike other hotels in the Condado, the Marriott has a great little beach right outside the door (be careful of the strong waves) with attentive beach staff that bring you chairs and drinks. There is a gay beach just a couple hundred yards away for those so inclined. For a Condado vacation -- this is the place to stay.

I instead insisted we be compensated and so they eventually offered us a free breakfast on the hotel which was not much to write home about! After much deliberation we were guaranteed the correct room the next morning, but it wasnt without me being somewhat pushy to get what we were entitled to. However, after our room switch the next morning the rest of our stay was quite enjoyable. We were placed on the 15th floor and the view was INCREDIBLE. Every night I sat out on the balcony from our room and just enjoyed listening to the waves crash and the clean night breeze. As for the hotel staff, I overall felt that they were not completely accomodating, but were helpful when questions needed to be answered (be aware that they do sometimes give falsified information IE: bus times and schedules). While there we ate at a few local restaurants and ventured over to the Wyndham hotel to check our the casino there (which is quite a step up from the Marriot). We did eat at Tuscany (in the Marriot) which was good food and good service (lots of seafood). I will definitely return to Puerto Rico in years to come...whether I stay at the Marriot is another question. I wouldn't shy away from staying there (esp with the private beach and nice pool), but would just be aware of the things I mentioned. If you stay there have a great time!Hope this helps! PS...As a plus I will say that everything was VERY clean.....

<Author>mpierce06
<Content>No regrets, but will stay elsewhere next time We were married sisters on a short vacation, stayed 5 nights. Room was nice, clean, and interesting view (16th floor) of both ocean and city. Yes, there is a lot of construction - but it's everywhere, not just around the Marriott. We enjoyed the 15 minutes/25-cent bus ride to Old San Juan, and you can board just one block from the hotel. The hotel seemed more appropriate for business travelers, and is definitely not where you want to be for a beach vacation - I would go out of town (Luquillo beach was beautiful) for that. Since we wanted to sightsee, we found the location to be fine, but there were several boutique hotels in the same area, for 1/3 the price, and including breakfast. The beach is public and easily accessed from anwhere along Ashford Ave, and you can rent a beach chair for $2. We chose Marriott since this was our first time to Puerto Rico, but now I know I can get good value for much less cost. You are paying for lobby entertainment, access to casino, and on-site restaurants. We only ate at the hotel once, for breakfast. There are great restaurants within walking distance - our favorite was the Waikiki, about 5 blocks west.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>A Nice Place to Stay We recently chose San Juan as a 4-day vacation spot to escape the freezing temperatures on the East Coast. We wanted the warmest weather with the shortest travel time, so we chose San Juan and stayed at the Marriott. That said, we were not disappointed, but we were not thrilled either. Everything was nice, but nothing was exceptional. However, we were so glad to be in such beautiful weather, it makes it hard to complain. The pool was nice, but yes, much of it is in the shade. The beach was nice, and they have an attendant who will strategically place your lounge chair so that you are in the sun (if you want to be). We ate at the poolside restaurant for breakfast and lunch. The food was good, not outstanding. A bit pricey, but that's what we expect when we go to a resort. The service was at times pretty bad (slow, brought wrong food, forgot items, etc.), but that doesn't bother us a whole lot because we're not in a hurry to get anywhere--we're just relaxing. One concierge was very helpful in suggesting local restaurants within walking distance (another concierge in training was pretty clueless). We tried a seafood restaurant called Miro--it was very good--better than the hotel restaurants. We liked the casino and the band, but older people may find the band too loud. My husband likes to gamble, and he thought the casino was great. Also--our room was nice, but nothing exceptional. We've definitely stayed in nicer resorts, but we did enjoy our stay at the Marriott--we just weren't blown away. I think we got what we were expecting, based on previous reviews. When the weather is so glorious, it's hard not to enjoy yourself!

<Content>Marriott lived up to its reputation We had a great experience at the Marriott for our January trip. Thanks to the previous travelers for your tips like the 25 cent bus ride to Old San Juan. I would also suggest taking a small back pack for water bottles, rain gear, etc. Most wives do not like their purses to be used as a carry all!  If you want something cheaper for a hotel but yet clean and safe- try the Holiday Inn Express nearby. They also offer a free continental breakfast.

<Author>TravelLover
<Content>Loved the San Juan Marriott We stayed at the Marriott Dec 17-19 for a precruise stay. We absolutely loved it! We paid $175 per night which included a full breakfast buffet for two each morning. The buffet was VERY good, but then again typical of Marriott breakfast buffets with the addition of excellent local tropical fruits. We had our breakfast each morning outside right next to the beach. . .had a wonderful view of the ocean. Our room was clean without any musty, moldy smell whatsoever. We were put in a cityview room (the hotel was completely booked so no upgrade) but on the eighteenth floor. When we stepped out onto our balcony we had a beautiful view of the ocean and beach! The balcony was fairly large with two lounge chairs and a table. It was glorious to have our coffee out on the balcony before heading down to the buffet.The staff were extremely friendly and helpful with tips on where to eat, where to buy bottled water etc. and how to get to Old San Juan inexpensively. We took the public transportation bus for 25 cents each. The bus stop was a half a block from the hotel and we were told that it ran every 30 minutes. We never waited more than 10 minutes. The bus took us down to a central bus terminal and then we hopped on a free trolley that took us around Old San Juan. We rode this a while to get our bearings. . .then got out and walked around. We walked on the Princessa (a beautiful pedestrian walkway that goes along the wall of the city). We also walked to El Morro (fort) which had beautiful views.The beach was very nice and clean. The ocean was very warm. . .I agree with a previous poster that it seemed to be warmer than the pool. My daughter (and husband) loved the water slide. They do have a beautiful hot tub which also had a waterfall flowing into it. . .of warm water. . .felt wonderful. They also had many poolside activities for kids and adults.Many people have commented on the noise in the lobby. I didn't find it excessive at all. It was great latin music which could only be heard in the lobby area itself. They also had a wonderful steel drum band by the pool. We had a great time recognizing traditional Christmas carols with a caribbean flair!In the Condado area, there were many restaurants and shops within walking distance, both local restaurants and chains such as Starbucks, Dunkin Donuts, Chilis, etc.We would not hesitate to stay at this hotel again!

<Content>Wonderful Hotel This hotel is wonderful! The views from your balcony are just spectacular. At night, you can see the lights from the cruise ships sailing along the ocean. We had dinner at Tiujana's twice. That restaurant is the best! The prices are also very reasonable. Great mexican food; burritos, tacos, enchaladas, margaritas. The waters and waitresses are extremly friendly and nice and all speak wonderful english. For lunch, we chose not to eat at the poolside cafe. Way too expenisve for a dumb burger. There are a Burger King, Wendy's, Subway, etc two blocks from the hotel. For breakfast we ate at Dunkin Donuts a couple blocks away from the hotel. We also went to a local market and bought some food which we kept in our room, while buying water at the Walgreens. We ate at Senor Frogs in Old San Juan one night because they were advertising everywhere, tourists had t-shirts on from there, and locals told us how great it was. We hated it. It was very much a local hangout. They had beer drinking competions and the food was simply burgers and frys. They also give you balloon hats to wear. The streets are not bad at all, and we did not experience any beggers along the streets anywhere, nor did we witness any animal cruelty. All locals are pretty nice, and most speek enough English to understand. I personally think San Juan is a gorgeous place to vacation and would definitly will come back to the San Juan Marriott.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>A Wonderful Experience! We stayed at this wonderful hotel for only one night (December 3, 2004) prior to a cruise, but we hope to go back again. The staff was friendly and helpful, especially when my sister-in-law reported her purse missing (it was recovered intact from the taxi where she had left it). Though we had booked city view, we were upgraded to ocean/pool view in a very secure wing. The rooms were clean, attractive, and comfortable (very good beds). With the high cost of accommodations in San Juan, the $175.00 per night we paid, which included a full buffet breakfast, was a good value. I booked directly with Marriott. We could have gotten a lower nonrefundable rate of $144.00 without breakfast, but decided against it. There is a friendly bar in the center of the lobby and a coffee shop (though there's also a Starbucks right across the street). The restaurant on the premises, Tuscany, is superb! We felt that the dinner we had was reasonably priced for food of such high quality. In fact, the pasta with lobster dish two of us chose was better than anything we had on our cruise--though the cruise line is well known for its cuisine. The casino is small and we didn't spend much time in it--we don't like smoky places. The grounds, pool, and beach are nice, and the Condado location is safe and convenient. The day we arrived, they had a special pre-Christmas festival, which the hotel participated in with a local church. It was a nice way to meet the locals. On the day of our cruise, the bell captain secured our luggage for us after checkout so that we could do some sightseeing before embarkation. I can see why the Marriott Resort is rated so highly, and concur with most of the other reviews I've read!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Decent hotel; Not enough sun Just returned from a 5 night stay. The location is great... There are stores and restaurants within walking distance... <Content>Mediocre Marriott Not great by Marriott's standards but probably the best in the Condado area. Hotel is old but rooms have been upgraded. Pool area is fantastic! Lively reception and casino. Nice Hertz desk on site and friendly staff. Once you see the hallways and rooms you'll wonder why you paid so much, but take a look around at the other Condado properties that are still in business and you'll realize you made the best choice. San Juan is not a premier destination and the Condado area seems to be declining. The new up and coming area is Isla Verde (Ritz, Interncontinental etc) by the airport. If you are determined to stay in Condado, this is your best bet.

<Author>groovedigger
<Content>Noisy? I call it lively ... Great experience if you want to be in the Condado area. You have to take a taxi to Old San Juan, but for the Condado zone it is very central, right on the beach. Exactly what you would expect from Marriott, friendly staff (they even upgraded me to a corner suite at no extra charge!), clean facilities, well-appointed rooms. Yes, the lobby is a big party scene every night with loud salsa music and crowds of revellers, but San Juan is a party place, folks! People do not go to bed at 10pm there ... remember you're not in Kansas anymore! If you're looking for a quiet isolated retreat or are simply too uptight about loud music, go to another part of the island. The casino is definitely nothing out of Las Vegas, but it has a decent selection of slot machines and blackjack tables, and usually a couple of roulette wheels operating. It is open 24 hours.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Perfect For Beach and City Interests We just returned from three nights at the Marriott Resort in the Condado section of San Juan. We were specifically looking for direct beach access and good proximity to old San Juan for dining and shopping We got all of this plus good places to eat in Condado (within walking distance of the hotel). The staff from the doormen, concerige to the maids were friendly and helpful. Our view could not be better and we slept with the baclony door open so we could hear the waves at night. There is a nightly salsa band in the lobby of the hotel and on the weekends there is lots of dancing. If this not your scene, request a room higher up or overlooking the pool/beach in a seperate wing so you will not be disturbed. Our room was clean, and other than a little tired wear on the paint on the balcony and in the bathroom, it was in acceptable condition. This is a beachfront property and in my experience there is always something about the rooms of hotels like this that no matter what, it will always have a slightly beachy wear to it (which is really no big deal.). Oh and did I mention the bed yet? It was one of the most comfortable hotel beds I've slept in (this includes the Westin chain's heavenly bed experience). It is true that some of the Condado strip is undergoing redevelopment from previous hurricane damage. There are two hotels on this particular strip of beach which are essentially being gutted but don't let this ruin your stay Other than the construction eye soar it should not disturb your stay. We were originally going to stay at the Ritz and they were full that weekend. And boy were we glad. The Ritz, while on Isle Verde and the water, also overlooks the main runway for the airport. While I am sure it is posh, I can't imagine being so close to the airport, particularly the main runway for take-off/landing (I spotted the Ritz and its signage from the window seat of my flight getting ready to take-off). Old San Juan is a $12 cab ride (flat fee to most places) and the airport is $15 one-way by taxi. If you want both beach and city activities the Marriott is the place to stay.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>This is a wonderful hotel Was sent to PR on business October 12-18, 2004, and took my husband along so that we could have a couple extra days of mini-vacation. Initially, I booked the Hampton Inn in Isla Verde, but my boss advised me to stay in Condado, as he thought the location would be more convenient -- not only for business (in Hato Rey), but for sightseeing, as well. I am SO glad I followed his advice! The Condado area is very safe and there are police and private security patrols everywhere you look. This gorgeous Marriott is right on the sand, centrally located in Condado, and a short taxi ride to Old San Juan (fare $12 one way). The hotel is beautiful, the staff is of the highest professional calibre (plus being very warm and friendly), and our stay couldn't have been better. Room Service was really quick (10-15 minutes!) with both morning coffee and midnight sandwiches. When you dial zero on the room phone (there are two), they answer the phone saying Good morning, Mrs.___, how may I be of service? (when was the last time you heard that in a hotel?) Housekeeping was efficient and the room was spotless.  The climate was humid, but the effect of the air conditioning was somewhat stymied by our insistence on keeping the sliding door to the balcony open at all times --- we couldn't resist the view of the pools/ocean from our 4th-floor Cabana room. My only negative comments would be that the live music (each night) was a little too loud in the downstairs area -- it was great music, but the noise-level made conversation in the whole foyer/bar/desk area close to impossible. Oh yes, and the Casino was adequate, but nowhere near Las Vegas standards. My husband went snorkeling off Fajardo one day on a 62-foot catamaran. The hotel tour desk booked the trip ($65 all inclusive) -- and he had a terrific time! Another day, we taxied out to the Bacardi Distillery ($25 one way) and took the tour, which includes two free drinks (try the Mojito). Both the Bacardi gift shop and the airport duty-free shop sell Bacardi rum at extremely reasonable prices and pack it securely to travel. If you stay at this Marriott, you will love it. Try Tijuana's Bar and Grill, also... it's down the street about a block and serves excellent Mexican food (I'm from LA and I know Mexican food! LOL). Puerto Rico es la Isla del encanto and I can hardly wait to go back!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>If I had to describe the Marriot in 1 word, 'Awesome' After deciding that I was going to go to Puerto Rico on a short notice vacation, I had asked a few people where to stay. My best friend who is Puerto Rican recommended the Marriot. He had been there about 2 months before us. We had also had gotten some feedback from others that stayed at other Hotels. My friend has very good taste so I took his word for this Hotel.After reading some reviews on trip advisor I started to wonder about his taste in Hotels, there were so many negative reviews that I began to wonder.We decided to go anyway and to our suprise the Hotel was everything he said it was. The rooms were clean and smelled like a hotel in the tropics should smell, like ocean air. And just like any other fancy hotel in the world if you use the room wet-bar you will be over charged, this is why they are there.Granted the Hotels restaurants were not cheap(priced accordingly) but if we had wanted to eat cheap food we could have gone to any of the many fast-food restaurants within walking distance. Which brings me to the next negative thing I had read, car rentals and parking. Renting a car was a great investment. If you were 4 people and had wanted to go on a guided tour it was easily $55-$95 per person. We had rented a brand new Toyota Corolla for $60 a day and can stay as long as we want any where we went. It is very hard to park in most towns but with patience we found great spots everywhere we went, and we went all over the Island. Now for the parking lot in the hotel. They charged us $12 for parking and you can go in and out within 24hours as much as you wanted to. To some this may sound like too much for guests in the hotel but after doing the math it is still cheaper. The best part was the absolutely perfect ocean water. After all the places me and my family had been too (which adds up to alot of places) we thought the ocean in Puerto Rico was possibly the best. I highly recommend one of the many Catamaran cruises with snorkeling and swimming, talk about being on a deserted desert Island in paradise (why did we come home???). ANd we were there during huricane season (it rained for about 1 hour the day we arrived, we had stayed 6 nights) all the other days were perfect 86-88 degrees and sunny.The food was also awesome, from traditional Puerto Rican food on the side of the road to one of the many gourmet restaurants in Old San Juan.Not to mention the service was exceptional. All in all we had a wonderful time and will definately be back to the Marriot.

<Author>Tomtopes
<Content>Good resort, just don't expect too much We stayed at the Marriott post cruise over the July 4th weekend and it was our second stay there. We loved the beach and its proximity to the airport and the service was good. We arrived at 9am and was given a corner suite even though the hotel was full. The rooms are just ok, (the air conditioner was pitiful, but made up for its lack of power with tremendous noise) but realistically, for a beach resort in San Juan, it is on the quality side. The biggest draw for us to the Marriott is the beach, being in the middle of Condado beach area is impressive. Just don't expect over the top service or immaculate rooms. The resort is just too big and always too full of guests for the staff to give personal or attentive service. The lobby is always hopping with locals enjoying their music and dances. During the July 4th weekend, a band was performing non stop salsa while locals were clearly enjoying themselves on the dancefloor. This is not a quiet and intimate hotel as the music level was so loud that we had to shout to speak with the front desk. Service at the coffee bar in the lobby was so slow that it was quicker to go across the street (careful not to be run over by maniac drivers on Ashford) to Starbucks. The pool area is a little crowded as they fit many sun loungers into a small space, but the beach is wide open. All around the hotel by the beachfront, the once derelict hotels to the West are being refurnished and the construction noise can be a distraction, but overall, the Marriott is a quality property in that stretch of Condado.

<Author>MoxieFan
<Content>Very Pleased With This Hotel Had a great stay in mid-March 2004. We were on the 19th floor with a half-ocean, half-city view. The room was always clean, but was small, with a comfortable bed and furnishings. Yes, the lobby rocks on weekend nights, and we stopped briefly to watch the dancing, though no one can talk above the music. However, we could not hear the lobby or casino sounds on our floor or in our room. Food in the Vista restaurant was very good; we did not try Anthony's. The lobby coffee shop makes excellent sandwiches and has great pasteries--at a fair price. There are many excellent restaurants within a block or two, a Walgreen's yards away for necessities, and a bus stop outside the hotel for the 15-minute (25 cents) ride to the old city. Every staff person we encountered was gracious, many asking whether there was anything we needed. The pool area was busy, but we always found lounge chairs somewhere. The large fountain pool, one of two pools, helps mask the people sounds, making poolside snoozes easy. Forget the hotel promo that you can swim laps in the pool; you can't. We stayed during very windy weather, so beach swimming was impossible. My only complaint is the amount of litter on the beach during the day; I blame careless guests. The beach is cleaned nightly. As other reviewers note, the Condado area has several derelict hotels, the lasting result of a devastating hurricane a few years ago. But elegant shops and a wide variety of restaurants on tree-lined Condado streets make up for a few blighted and under-construction areas. We would definitely go back.

<Author>Ron_Bartizek
<Content>In the middle of everything Don't worry about those negative ratings, this is a great place to stay if you want to do more than hang out at the hotel for a week. We had two adults and three teenagers, and everyone (almost, except a bored 14-year-old boy) had a great time. The hotel is clean, facilities are more than adequate and the staff is friendly and helpful. If you don't want to go out, the lobby offers music almost every night. Not sure about the hotel food, because we only ate one dinner there. Several excellent and varied restaurants are within walking distance, and there's a public bus stop right outside (25 cents!), so it's easy and trouble-free getting to Old San Juan for even more dining and entertainment options. Oh, our rooms (2) looked over the pool and to the ocean, and were very quiet - no noisy pool activity was evident. This isn't really a resort, but the setting more than makes up for any shortcomings.

<Author>manycruises
<Content>Wonderful hotel, the Marriott Since I had read other reviews of this hotel on your website (both pro and anti), I was curious to see how we would like the hotel. We loved it! We were given a tenth floor room facing the ocean. We were thoroughly entertained watching the activity on the beach when we were not actually there ourselves. The hotel was immaculately clean, the personnel were very friendly and helpful, and the food in the restaurant was excellent. There is a tour desk in the lobby for booking activities outside the hotel. The hotel itself provides a full day of planned activities if you are looking for something to do. Our travel agent found a special weekend rate for senior citizens that was a wonderful deal. This is not just a hotel for senior citizens. Indeed, we were in the distinct minority with many young couples and family groups too. The Condado area is the resort spot of San Juan, and this hotel is located right in the middle of the area with a gorgeous beach. I wish we could have stayed longer.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>A fantastic business trip I stayed at the Marriott Resort  Stellaris Casino on a recent business trip to San Juan. The hotel was very nice. The location was fantastic short cab rides to the airport, downtown, and Old San Juan. The street in front of the hotel (Asheford Avenue) was always lively and there were many great shops and restaurants, plus a delicious gelato shop across the street. The pool was beautiful, although crowded. It had fountains, a mountain waterslide, and pool bar. The beach chairs around the pool were all fitted with comfortable cushions. This hotel also had a fantastic gym - lots of machines and weights to plug head sets into - not your typical hotel weight room. The room was great, very clean. One upstairs hallway had a bit of a humid, dank feeling to it, but I guess thats typical in tropics. I loved the little coffee shop in the lobby - an excellent alternative to a $10 hotel breakfast. The casino downstairs meant that the lobby was bumpin at night. On several occasions there was a VERY loud live band playing, but it didnt disturb me on the 9th floor. The beach wasnt great by Caribbean standards, but thats not the hotel's fault. The hotel was very good about providing beach chairs, and there was a security guard stationed at the hotel entrance to the beach keeping an eye on things. The water was clean and many people were goofing around with bogie boards in the surf - I guess there was somewhere to rent these close by. This is a public beach, as I understand all beaches are in San Juan. Occasionally someone would walk by selling water, or necklaces, or ice cream, but it wasnt overwhelming. The staff, especially the concierge, were all very nice and helpful.

<Author>Liteh
<Content>A Comfortable Enough Stay Stayed here for a few days the week before Christmas (there was even a pretty holiday spread, with gingerbread houses, in the front of the lobby). After reading the other reviews, I had been worried that I would be disturbed by noise from the lobby at night. As it turned out, there were nice live band shows and dancing in the lobby several nights during my stay, but I didn't hear any noise from my 5th floor room and wasn't distracted by the music whenever I passed through the lobby. I think some of the other reviewers have exaggerated the signs of wear about the hotel. It may be older, but seems to be holding up pretty well, especially in the public areas. If you decide to stay here, pay a little more to get a corner room; I was shocked by how small my standard oceanview room, ordered blindly through one of the online sites, was (and even the maid acknowledged it was one of the smaller rooms). The room was very clean, but there was a slightly annoying smell of mold (common in my experience in some of the Caribbean islands) the first few days. A plus for me was the pretty well-equipped fitness room. I have stayed in several hotels in San Juan over the years, including the Ritz, the Old San Juan Wyndham, and several smaller, independent hotels. Personally, I prefer the Condado hotels for trips when I am not renting a car because there are more clubs and reasonably-priced restaurants within walking distance than in Old San Juan and Isla Verde. And, if it's any indication of anything about the hotel, most of the other guests I saw in the public areas and on the beach seemed to be enjoying themselves.

<Author>nrn0896
<Content>Pleased with the stay I went to this property as an experiment because I normally favor hotels with ready golf course accessibility. My only caution is that the Atlantic surf at the beach is moderate to immoderate -- not placid like many Caribbean hotels, but not different from most of the other San Juan hotels. This may be a disappointment to those with small children (who may be content with the adequate pool and water slide) or to certain adults whose water skills may not be up to the task. This was the only potential drawback to a really good experience.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>No longer venerable My wife and I have spent hundreds of nights at this Marriott over the past 7 years. It was never a top-line property, but it was well run and pleasant to visit. That has changed.We recently finished a 5 month continuous stint at SJM, and it was clear that things have gone off the track. We occupied several rooms during that time, the first being a large penthouse suite. It was a mold nightmare as each time it rained the water flooded a considerable area inside the 2 balcony doors. Management knew of the problem and did nothing to eliminate it. (Since then they are apparently replacing the exterior doors of the high-rise section.) Another room had a toilet that had to be plunged on 15 different days before the maid -- who said this had been happening long before we stayed in the room -- convinced engineering the replace the commode. Every time the toilet was unplugged the remnants of an oft-used plunger left drippings in the bathroom, and it was up to us to call housecleaning to deal with the residual fecal matter. Ugh! (Before we stayed on the penthouse floor we were shown another room which we declined because there was a hole punched in the balcony door and the a/c didn't work. The hotel's a/c is quite awful and it seems that engineering is incapable of improving it.)When we first arrived, after having been gone about a year, we were startled to discover that the Executive Lounge was no longer open on weekends. I spoke to the GM, and he agreed to reopen it. Until the day we left, the hotel was never able to get anyone to restock the refrigerator with soft drinks or keep the room clean. The management was content to let the guests -- mostly this one -- do the restocking, and leave the cleaning for the weekday staff. Months of pleading and complaining fell on deaf ears. When I griped to the GM about my having to restock the fridge his response was a sneering Don't do it! Under prior management the lounge was always well-tended on weekends.The decline of the SJM is nowhere more evident than the front desk. The friendly rapid-response is now very hit and miss. One time I told a desk supervisor that I needed to speak to her about something, and she said she would call. Later the same day I passed by and asked her if she had forgotten, which she said she had not. She may not have forgotten but I never got a call. Senior management is well aware of the problems, but seems unwilling to rectify them.SJM has a facsimile of a concierge compared to the past and to other hotels. They often refer guests to a subcontracted tour desk which gives guests materials brought over from the Hilton.There are some fine and pleasant employees, but morale seems to be lower than we've seen it. Some of the best employees privately confide that they don't enjoy working at the SJM anymore. For many it seems like just a job, with little of the pride and enthusiasm from the past.There is an arrogance among managers that was not visible under previous regimes. Some of the senior managers act like they are the important part of the hotel, rather than the guests.Since we left the SJM and moved to another hotel, we've been happier. Management reponds quickly and efficiently to problems, the a/c works, and we don't have to deal with management arrogance.

<Content>So-so hotel in downscale district The staff is mostly friendly but the service is slipshod. Maid service runs from mediocre to poor. Room service is awful. The place looks pretty rundown, and the rooms are in second-rate shape. Nice pools and pool staff. The adjoining public beach is filthy. The neighborhood is in poor shape, with some good restaurants and not much else. Hotel restaurants are OK with friendly staff, but they are badly organized with unnecessary congestion, esp. on weekends.  
<Date>Sep 2, 2003
<Rating>2	-1	-1	-1	-1	-1	-1	-1	

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great and fun time We researched many hotels as to the beach involved. My boyfriend and I wanted to hear the waves at night and walk out to the beach when we wanted. We found the Marriott CasinoResort (Condado area) to be the one! After we got there, we toured many other hotels. I am also a travel agent, outside sales. I was very glad we chose the Marriott. Their beach is everything they said it was. In fact, not many of the other hotels had much of a beach at all. We left our door open at night and listened to the waves. We had no problems with mosquitos or flies. The hotel's buffet for dinner was just OK. But their breakfast buffet was really good. We found a Mexican restaurant, 6 blks away, toward Old San Juan that was wonderful. It was the only one I saw on Condado Beach. I would really like to go to the island of Viequess just off Puerto Rico on my next visit. They have a beautiful beach all the way around island. The tour of Old San Juan was great. Overall, the people were fabulous. We never met anyone that wasn't pleasnt and fun to ask questions. Many families were out for Sundays which is better than what we see in the US mainland. Overall, we went before and after a cruise. I would definitely like to go back to Puerto Rico and spend a week, touring their island more. It was much prettier than some of the islands on the cruise itinerary. Loved it overall!  
<Date>Jul 22, 2003
